Condition of a City (Misr) for Friday Prayer
Explaining the condition of a city for Jumu'ah and its definitional disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition of a city (misr) for Jumu'ah, identify the proof from Ali, and distinguish between the definitions of misr according to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is valid only in a major city (misr jami') — the condition is proven by the saying of Ali, but the exact definition of misr varies among Hanafi imams.

Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) has conditions for obligation and conditions for performance. One of the most important conditions for performance is that it be held in a city (misr), not in a village or desert. This lesson examines the textual proof for this condition and the intra-Hanafi discussion on what constitutes a misr. Understanding this clarifies when Jumu'ah becomes valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its category
Recognize that the misr condition is a condition for performance (shart al-ada'), not obligation. A missing condition for performance renders the prayer invalid.
Performance conditions are external to the person.
2
Locate the primary proof
Find the saying of Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا صلاة فطر ولا أضحى إلا في مصر جامع' (No Jumu'ah, no tashriq, no Eid prayers except in a major city). This is the Hanafi dalil.
This is a qawl sahabi, which is a proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab response
Shafi'i argues using the hadith of Ibn Abbas that Jumu'ah was held in a village mosque in Jawazi, Bahrain. The Hanafi response is that Jawazi is actually a fortress city, and the term 'village' is used loosely (as in the Quran).
The Hanafi response refutes the opposing proof by reinterpreting the hadith's setting.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi definitions
Abu Hanifa defines misr as a town with streets, markets, outlying villages, a just ruler, and a scholar. Abu Yusuf defines it as a place with an amir and qadi who enforce hadd penalties. Muhammad considers that if the adhan is heard in a village, Jumu'ah is valid. The commentator prefers Abu Hanifa's definition as the most correct.
These definitions affect when Jumu'ah becomes valid in smaller settlements.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's definition, as the commentator states 'وهو الأصح' (it is the most correct). Therefore, Jumu'ah is valid only in a city meeting all of Abu Hanifa's criteria.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرط أدائها : اعلم أن لوجوبها شرائط، وهي في المصلى كما سيأتي، ولأدائها شرائط، وهي في غير المصلى، والفرق بين شرائط الوجوب وشرائط الأداء: أن بانتفاء الأول يصح الأداء، وبانتفاء الثاني لا يصح، ونظم بعضهم شروط الأداء والوجوب فقال: حر يعني صحيح بالبلوغ مذكر مقيم وذو عقل لشرط وجوبها ومصر وسلطان ووقت وخطبة وإذن كذا جمع لشرط أدائها والحاصل: أن شرائط الأداء أيضاً ستة: الأول: المصر فلم تجز في قرية على الصحيح، وعن أبي يوسف القرية إن كانت داخل السور فعلى أهلها الجمعة، وإلا فلا وعن محمد كل قرية يسمع أهلها الأذان فعليهم الجمعة، خلافاً للشافعي؛ لحديث ابن عباس لما أنها أقيمت بمسجد عبد القيس بجوائي قرية من قرى البحرين، ولنا: قول علي انه "لا جمعة ولا تشريق" إلى آخره، ولا حجة له في حديث ابن عباس هما؛ لأن جوائي اسم لحصن بالبحرين، وهي مدينة والمدينة تسمى قرية كما ورد في القرآن (مسكين، فتح المصر فلا تجوز في قرية ولا مفازة؛ لقول علي : لا جمعة ولا تشريق ولا صلاة فطر ولا أضحى إلا في مصر جامع. (ط،ع) أمير وقاض: يحرس الناس ويمنع المفسدين ويقوي أحكام الشرع. (ع) ويقيم الحدود: [هذا عند أبي يوسف وهو الصحيح، وفي رواية عنه المصر الجامع كل موضع أهلها كثير بحيث لو اجتمعوا في أكبر مساجدهم لم يسعهم. (عيني)] أي يرجم المحصن الزاني، ويجلد غير المحصن، ويقطع السارق، ويحد القاذف وشارب الخمر، ويحكم بالقود والدية ونحوها، وتفسير المصر بكل موضع له أمير إلخ رواية عن أبي يوسف وهو ظاهر المذهب، وهو الصحيح، وعليه أكثر الفقهاء، وقال أبو حنيفة: المصر كل بلدة فيها سكك ،وأسواق ولها رساتيق يعني القرى، ووال ينصف المظلوم من ظالمه وعالم يرجع إليه في الحوادث وهو الأصح وقيل في تفسير المصر أقوال أخر، وأحسن ما قيل فيه: إذا كان أهلها بحال لو اجتمعوا في أكبر مساجدهم لم يسعهم، وهو رواية عن الثاني. (فتح، مستخلص)
Condition of its performance: Know that there are conditions for its obligation and conditions for its performance. The conditions for obligation are in the person praying as will come, and the conditions for performance are external. The difference: if the conditions for obligation are absent, the performance is valid (if done), but if the conditions for performance are absent, it is not valid. Some have arranged the conditions of performance and obligation in verse: 'Free, meaning valid, with puberty, male, resident, and intelligence are conditions for obligation; and a city, a sultan, time, a sermon, and permission, thus gathered are conditions for performance.' The summary: The conditions for performance are six: First: the city (al-misr). So it is not valid in a village according to the correct position. From Abu Yusuf: if the village is within the wall, then its inhabitants must perform Jumu'ah, otherwise not. From Muhammad: every village that can hear the adhan, its inhabitants must perform Jumu'ah, contrary to al-Shafi'i due to the hadith of Ibn Abbas that it was established in the mosque of 'Abd al-Qays in Jawazi, a village of Bahrain. Our proof is the saying of Ali: 'No Jumu'ah nor tashriq' etc. There is no proof for him in the hadith of Ibn Abbas because Jawazi is the name of a fortress in Bahrain, which is a city, and a city is called a village as in the Quran. Al-Misr: it is not valid in a village nor in a desert due to the saying of Ali: 'No Jumu'ah nor tashriq nor Eid al-Fitr nor Eid al-Adha except in a major city (misr jami').' A ruler and judge: protects people and prevents corruption and enforces the laws of Shariah. And establishes hadd punishments: this is according to Abu Yusuf and it is the correct view. In another narration from him: the comprehensive city is every place whose inhabitants are numerous such that if they gathered in their largest mosque, it would not contain them. i.e., he stones the married adulterer, flogs the unmarried, cuts off the hand of the thief, punishes the slanderer and the wine drinker, and judges retaliation, blood money, etc. The interpretation of misr as every place having an amir etc. is a narration from Abu Yusuf and it is the apparent position of the madhhab, and it is correct, and it is the opinion of most jurists. Abu Hanifa said: The city (misr) is every town that has streets and markets and has outlying villages (rasatiq), and a guardian who does justice to the oppressed from his oppressor, and a scholar to refer to in incidents, and this is the most correct. It was also said in interpretation of misr other sayings, and the best that was said: that its inhabitants are such that if they gathered in their largest mosque, it would not contain them, and that is a narration from the second (Abu Yusuf).
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the conditions for Friday prayer, specifically the condition of performance that it must be in a city (misr). The commentator begins by distinguishing between conditions for obligation (shurut al-wujub) and conditions for performance (shurut al-ada'). Conditions for obligation relate to the individual (such as freedom, sanity, puberty, maleness, residence), while conditions for performance relate to the external environment. He then presents a poetic summary of both sets of conditions, attributed to some scholar. For the performance, the first condition is al-misr (the city). The commentator states that Jumu'ah is not valid in a village on the correct view. He then reports the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on villages: Abu Yusuf restricts it to walled villages, while Muhammad extends it to any village that hears the adhan. These views are presented against al-Shafi'i's position that Jumu'ah is valid even in villages, citing the hadith of Ibn Abbas that Jumu'ah was held in a village mosque in Bahrain. The Hanafi response is that Jawazi is actually a fortress, i.e., a city, and the term 'village' (qarya) in the Quran can refer to a city. The definitive proof for the Hanafi position is the saying of Ali ibn Abi Talib: 'No Jumu'ah, no tashriq, no Eid al-Fitr, no Eid al-Adha except in a major city (misr jami').' This is a qawl sahabi (companion's statement) which is considered a proof in Hanafi usul. Then the commentator discusses the definition of misr. He gives the view of Abu Yusuf: a place with an amir and qadi who implement laws and enforce hadd penalties. He also reports another narration from Abu Yusuf defining it as a place so populous that the largest mosque cannot contain all residents. Abu Hanifa's definition is a town with streets, markets, and outlying villages, and with a just guardian and a scholar for rulings. The commenter considers Abu Hanifa's view the most correct. He also mentions that the best definition is the one from the second narration of Abu Yusuf (population size). This passage contains an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and his students on the definition of misr. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but the commentator notes that Abu Yusuf's first narration (amir and qadi) is the apparent position of the madhhab and is correct.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A major city with a ruler, judge, markets, and outlying areas; the specific Hanafi definition is debated.
قرية (qarya): A village, as opposed to a city. Hanafis require a city, not a village.
تشريق (tashriq): The takbirs recited after Eid prayers; here it refers to the Eid prayers themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi proof that Jumu'ah requires a city (misr)?
A) Hadith of Ibn Abbas
B) Saying of Ali (لا جمعة إلا في مصر جامع)
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Quranic verse

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires Jumu'ah to be held in a major city (misr jami') as proven by the saying of Ali, but the definition of misr varies between Abu Hanifa and his students.

The Musalla and Precinct (Fina') for Jumu'ah
Explaining the extension of the city to the musalla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Jumu'ah in the musalla and explain the estimation of the precinct (fina').

Core Idea
Hanafis permit Jumu'ah in all city open spaces; the precinct is estimated at one farsakh.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on the location of Friday prayer. The school expands the valid area beyond the central mosque to include the musalla (prayer ground) and all open areas that serve the city's needs. The key concept is the 'fina'' (precinct), which is annexed to the city. The chosen view for fatwa is that the fina' extends one farsakh from the city limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The passage discusses the musalla (prayer ground) of the city and its ruling for Jumu'ah. It states that Jumu'ah is not restricted to the mosque but can be performed in the musalla and all open spaces (afniyah) of the city.
2
Understand the concept of fina'
The fina' (precinct) is the area around the city used for its needs. It is legally considered part of the city. The passage gives examples: galloping horses, gathering armies, funeral prayer, and burying the dead.
These needs show the practical extension of the city.
3
Note the chosen estimation
The chosen position for fatwa is Muhammad's view that the fina' is estimated at one farsakh (approx. 5.5 km). This means Jumu'ah is valid anywhere within that radius.
Other opinions existed, but this is mufta bihi.
4
Relate to Eid prayer
The passage draws an analogy: just as the city and fina' are conditions for Jumu'ah, they are also conditions for Eid prayer. Thus, the same spatial rules apply.
Eid prayer is also performed in the musalla.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو مصلاه: [وهو ما حوله لمصالحه مطلقاً، والمختار للفتوى تقديره بفرسخ. (ط)] الحكم غير مقصور على المصلى، بل تجوز الجمعة في جميع أفنية المصر؛ لأنها بمنزلة في حق حوائج أهل المصر من ركض الخيل وجمع العساكر وصلاة الجنازة ودفن الموتى ونحو ذلك، والمختار للفتوى قول محمد أنه مقدر بفرسخ، الحاصل: أنه تؤدى الجمعة في مصلى المصر مثل مصلى العيد سواء كان بينهما مزارع أولا ؛ لأنه يكون في فنائه، وفناؤه ملحق به، وكما أن المصر وفناؤه شرط جواز الجمعة، فهو شرط جواز صلاة العيد. (عيني، مسكين) ومناً مصر: [فتجوز إقامة الجمعة فيها إذا كان الإمام أمير الحجاز أو الخليفة لا أمير الموسم؛ لأنه يلي أمور الحج لا غير. (ط،ع)] وقال محمد: لا تجوز؛ لأنها من القرى ولهما أنها تتمصر في أيام الموسم، وفيها أبنية ودور وسكك، وهذا يشير إلى أنها لا تجوز في غير أيام الموسم؛ لأنها لا تبقى مصراً بعدها، وقيل: تجوز؛ لأنها مكة بناء على تقدير الفناء بفرسخين، لكن تقدير الفناء بذلك غير صحيح. (عيني، فتح) لا عرفات: [ أي هي ليست بمصر؛ لأنها فناء ولا من فناء مكة (ع)] ولو كان الخليفة بها في قولهم جميعاً، وهي علم للموقف ولكنها منصرف كمسلمات؛ لأن الألف والتاء تمنع تقدير تاء التأنيث فيها، والتي فيها ليست الألف علامة جمع المؤنث سميت بذلك؛ لأنها وصفت لإبراهيم عليه، فلما أبصرها عرفها، هي مع التأنيث إنما وقيل: التقى فيها آدم وحواء عليهما السلام فتعارفا، وقيل: غير ذلك. (فتح)
Or his musalla: i.e., the area around it for its needs absolutely, and the chosen position for fatwa is that it is estimated by a farsakh. The ruling is not restricted to the musalla; rather Jumu'ah is permissible in all the open spaces (afniyah) of the city because they are like the city regarding the needs of the inhabitants such as galloping horses, gathering armies, funeral prayer, and burying the dead and the like. The chosen for fatwa is the saying of Muhammad that it is estimated by a farsakh. The conclusion: Jumu'ah is performed in the musalla of the city like Eid prayer, whether there are farmlands between them or not, because it is in its precinct (fina'), and its precinct is annexed to it. Just as the city and its precinct are conditions for the validity of Jumu'ah, so are they conditions for the validity of Eid prayer. And Mina is a city: it is permissible to hold Jumu'ah there if the imam is the amir of the Hijaz or the caliph, not the amir of the season (amir al-mawsim) because he only handles Hajj affairs. Muhammad said it is not permissible because it is a village. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that it becomes a city during the season of Hajj, having buildings, houses, and streets. This indicates that it is not permissible outside the season because it does not remain a city afterwards. It was said it is permissible because it is part of Mecca based on estimating the fina' at two farsakhs, but that estimation is not correct. Not Arafat: i.e., it is not a city because it is an open space (fina') and not part of the fina' of Mecca, even if the caliph is there, according to all of them. It is a proper noun for the standing place but it is declinable like Muslims, because the alif and ta prevent the ta of femininity. It is named Arafat because it was described to Abraham; when he saw it, he recognized it. Or it is said that Adam and Eve met there and recognized each other.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage discusses two further issues related to the location of Friday prayer. First, the musalla (prayer ground) of the city: The commentator states that Jumu'ah is not restricted to the central mosque; it can be performed in the musalla (open space outside the city used for Eid) and in all the open spaces (afniyah) of the city. The reason is that these spaces serve the needs of the inhabitants such as military training, collecting armies, funerals, etc. The correct view for fatwa is that the musalla area is estimated at one farsakh (about 5.5 km) from the city, according to Muhammad. The commentator draws an analogy with Eid prayer: just as the city and its precinct (fina') are conditions for Jumu'ah, they are conditions for Eid prayer. Second, Mina: There is a dispute regarding Jumu'ah in Mina during Hajj. The Hanafi position is that Jumu'ah can be held in Mina if the ruling authority is the caliph or the amir of the Hijaz, not the amir of the season (who only oversees Hajj). Muhammad holds it is not permissible because Mina is a village. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) consider it becomes a city temporarily during the Hajj season due to the abundance of buildings and people. The commentator notes that this implies it is only permissible during the season. Another opinion states it is permissible because Mina is within the two-farsakh precinct of Mecca, but this estimation is rejected. Third, Arafat: Arafat is not a city, so Jumu'ah cannot be held there even if the caliph is present. Arafat is an open space and not part of Mecca's precinct. The passage ends with linguistic notes on the name Arafat.

Key Terms
مصلى (musalla): The prayer ground outside the city, used for Eid and also for Jumu'ah.
فناء (fina'): The precinct or surrounding area of a city, annexed to it for purposes like Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the chosen estimation for the precinct (fina') of a city for Jumu'ah?
A) Half a farsakh
B) One farsakh
C) Two farsakhs
D) No estimation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits Jumu'ah in the musalla and all open spaces of the city's precinct, estimated at one farsakh.

Mina and Arafat: Their Status for Jumu'ah
Status of Mina and Arafat for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on Jumu'ah in Mina during Hajj and the ruling on Arafat, including the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Mina is valid for Jumu'ah only during Hajj season; Arafat is never valid.

Building on the previous lesson, this lesson addresses two special locations near Mecca: Mina and Arafat. The Hanafi school recognizes that Mina becomes a city temporarily during the Hajj season due to the influx of people and buildings, allowing Jumu'ah if the imam is the caliph or amir of Hijaz. Arafat, however, remains an open space and cannot host Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Jumu'ah requires a city (misr) or its precinct (fina'). Mina is a question: is it a city?
2
Examine Mina
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two), Mina becomes a city during the Hajj season due to buildings and streets. Therefore, Jumu'ah is valid then, provided the imam is the caliph or amir of Hijaz (not the amir al-mawsim who only handles Hajj).
Muhammad's other view says it is a village and invalid.
3
Note Muhammad's objection
Muhammad (in one narration) says Jumu'ah is not valid because Mina is originally a village (qaryah), not a city.
This shows an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze Arafat
Arafat is not a city; it is an open space (fina') and not even part of Mecca's fina'. Thus, Jumu'ah is invalid there even if the caliph is present.
The passage gives linguistic notes on the name Arafat.
5
Understand the imam condition
For Mina, the imam must be the caliph or amir of Hijaz (who has authority over the region), not just the amir of the Hajj season. This condition is specific to Mina.
This extra condition is not mentioned for Arafat, but Arafat is invalid anyway.

منى (mina): A location near Mecca; its status as a city is disputed for Jumu'ah.
عرفات (arafat): A plain near Mecca where Hajj standing occurs; not a city for Jumu'ah.
أمير الموسم (amir al-mawsim): The official in charge of Hajj affairs, distinct from the ruler.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Multiple Jumu'ah Congregations in a City
Ruling on multiple Jumu'ah locations with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the number of Jumu'ah congregations in one city and identify the conditions for multiple locations.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits two Jumu'ah congregations in a city, but not more.

This passage addresses a practical concern: when a city becomes large, can Jumu'ah be held in more than one place? The Hanafi masters differ, but the relied-upon view from Zahir al-Riwayah limits it to two. We will explore the proofs and conditions that govern this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key issue
Determine the legal question: In how many locations within one city can Jumu'ah prayer be validly performed?
2
State the views of the three Hanafi masters
List the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani as reported in the text.
3
Understand the relied-upon position
The text declares that in Zahir al-Riwayah, two locations are permissible and more than two are not, and 'upon this is reliance'.
4
Analyze the proof
The evidence is the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib, who would go to the graveyard for Eid and leave a deputy to pray with the weak in the city.
5
Apply the condition
Note the condition mentioned by Abu Yusuf: a large river without a bridge, or a very large city, for multiple locations to be allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في مواضع أي في موضعين أو ثلاثة عند محمد، وعن أبي يوسف روايتان في رواية لا يجوز إلا إذا كان بين موضعين نهر عظيم فيصير بمنزلة مصرين وقيل شرط أيضاً أن لا يكون على النهر جسر أو كان ولكن يأمر بقطع الجسر الجمعة حتى ينقطع الوصل، وفي رواية قال: يجوز إذا كان المصر عظيماً في موضعين، ولم يجز يوم في الثلاث، فإن أدوها في موضعين فالجمعة لمن سبق منهما وللآخرين أن يعيدوا الظهر، وإن أدوها معاً أو كان لا يدرى كيف كان يجوز صلاتهم، وروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجوز الجمعة في الموضعين أو أكثر وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز في موضعين ولا يجوز في أكثر من ذلك وعليه الاعتماد، فإنه روي أن علياً كان يخرج إلى الجبانة في العيد ويستخلف في المصر من يصلي بضعفة الناس وذلك بمحضر من الصحابة فلما جاز في صلاة العيد جاز في الجمعة؛ لأنهما في الاختصاص بالمصر يستويان. (فتح، مستخلص) تتمة: سئل السيد الحموي عن أربع ركعات التي بعد صلاة الجمعة وتسمى الظهر عندهم إذا اختلت بعض شروط الجمعة هل هي فرض أو واجبة أو مستحبة أو ليست بواحدة منها وما كيفية نية الظهر على القول بها؟ فأجاب بأنها ليست فرضا ولا واجبة ولا سنة، بل ولا أصل لها في المذهب، وقال في البحر: وقد أفتيت مراراً بعدم صلاتها خوفاً على اعتقاد الجهلة أنها الفرض وأن الجمعة ليست بفرض. (فتح، مستخلص)
In multiple locations: i.e., in two or three according to Muhammad. From Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one narration, it is not permissible unless there is a great river between the two locations, making them like two cities, and it is also a condition that there be no bridge over the river, or if there is, the imam orders the bridge to be cut off during the Friday prayer so that connection is severed. In another narration, he said: it is permissible if the city is large, in two locations, and not more than three. If they perform it in two locations, the Jumu'ah goes to whichever of them preceded, and the others must perform Zuhr if they are not sure which was first. If they performed it simultaneously or it is unknown, both are valid. Muhammad reports from Abu Hanifa that it is permissible in two or more locations. In the apparent riwayah, it is permissible in two but not in more, and this is the relied-upon position. It is narrated that Ali used to go out to the graveyard for Eid and would leave someone behind to pray with the weak people, and this was in the presence of the Companions. So when it is permissible in Eid prayer, it is permissible in Jumu'ah because both are equal in being specific to the city. Appended: Al-Sayyid al-Hamawi was asked about the four rak'ats after Jumu'ah, which they call Zuhr, when some conditions of Jumu'ah are lacking: is it fard, wajib, mustahabb, or none? He answered that it is not fard, not wajib, not sunnah, and it has no basis in the madhhab. In al-Bahr, it is reported: I have given fatwa many times against praying it, for fear that the ignorant might believe that it is the obligation and that Jumu'ah is not the fard.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage addresses two distinct issues. First, the validity of holding Jumu'ah in multiple locations within the same city. The commentators present the views of Muhammad, Abu Yusuf, and Abu Hanifa. According to Muhammad, it is permissible in two or three locations. Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one requiring a large river between locations with no bridge to ensure they are effectively separate cities; another allowing two locations if the city is large, but not three. The apparent riwayah (Zahir al-Riwayah) from Abu Hanifa permits two but not more, and this is the relied-upon position. The proof is the practice of Ali, who would go to the graveyard for Eid and leave a deputy to pray with the weak in the city, implying multiple congregations are permissible. Second, the passage ends with a fatwa from al-Sayyid al-Hamawi regarding the four rak'ats after Jumu'ah, sometimes called the Zuhr prayer. Some people pray these rak'ats out of caution when conditions of Jumu'ah are lacking. The fatwa states that this practice has no basis in the Hanafi madhhab; it is not fard, wajib, or sunnah. The commentator warns that praying these rak'ats might lead the ignorant to believe that the real obligation is these four rak'ats and that Jumu'ah is not the fard, which is a dangerous innovation.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known transmission from Abu Hanifa through his students.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, how many Jumu'ah congregations may be held in one city?
A) Only one
B) Two
C) Three
D) As many as needed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits two Jumu'ah congregations in a large city, subject to conditions, but no more than two.

The Four Rak'ats After Jumu'ah: A Baseless Practice
Fatwa against post-Jumu'ah four rak'ats

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the four rak'ats after Jumu'ah have no basis in the Hanafi madhhab and identify the potential danger of this practice.

Core Idea
The four rak'ats after Jumu'ah are not fard, wajib, or sunnah, and praying them can undermine the obligation of Jumu'ah.

This passage from the end of the chapter addresses a common practice: some people pray four rak'ats after Jumu'ah, calling it 'Zuhr', especially when conditions of Jumu'ah are lacking. The Hanafi scholars explicitly reject this practice as having no foundation in the madhhab, warning it may lead the ignorant to doubt the obligation of Jumu'ah itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the practice being questioned
Some people pray four rak'ats after Jumu'ah, sometimes called the 'Zuhr' prayer, especially when Jumu'ah conditions are lacking.
2
State the answer of al-Sayyid al-Hamawi
He was asked about its ruling and replied it is not fard, not wajib, not sunnah, and has no basis in the madhhab.
3
Understand the reason for the fatwa
The commentator in al-Bahr says he gave fatwa against it out of fear that ignorant people might think these four rak'ats are the obligation and that Jumu'ah is not fard.
4
Recognize the danger
This practice can lead to a dangerous innovation: believing that the real obligation is the four rak'ats, thus undermining the obligation of Jumu'ah.
5
Apply the ruling
The correct position is that after Jumu'ah, one may pray sunnah prayers (like the regular sunnah of Zuhr) but not a specifically prescribed four-rak'at prayer called 'Zuhr' as a replacement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في مواضع أي في موضعين أو ثلاثة عند محمد، وعن أبي يوسف روايتان في رواية لا يجوز إلا إذا كان بين موضعين نهر عظيم فيصير بمنزلة مصرين وقيل شرط أيضاً أن لا يكون على النهر جسر أو كان ولكن يأمر بقطع الجسر الجمعة حتى ينقطع الوصل، وفي رواية قال: يجوز إذا كان المصر عظيماً في موضعين، ولم يجز يوم في الثلاث، فإن أدوها في موضعين فالجمعة لمن سبق منهما وللآخرين أن يعيدوا الظهر، وإن أدوها معاً أو كان لا يدرى كيف كان يجوز صلاتهم، وروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجوز الجمعة في الموضعين أو أكثر وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز في موضعين ولا يجوز في أكثر من ذلك وعليه الاعتماد، فإنه روي أن علياً كان يخرج إلى الجبانة في العيد ويستخلف في المصر من يصلي بضعفة الناس وذلك بمحضر من الصحابة فلما جاز في صلاة العيد جاز في الجمعة؛ لأنهما في الاختصاص بالمصر يستويان. (فتح، مستخلص) تتمة: سئل السيد الحموي عن أربع ركعات التي بعد صلاة الجمعة وتسمى الظهر عندهم إذا اختلت بعض شروط الجمعة هل هي فرض أو واجبة أو مستحبة أو ليست بواحدة منها وما كيفية نية الظهر على القول بها؟ فأجاب بأنها ليست فرضا ولا واجبة ولا سنة، بل ولا أصل لها في المذهب، وقال في البحر: وقد أفتيت مراراً بعدم صلاتها خوفاً على اعتقاد الجهلة أنها الفرض وأن الجمعة ليست بفرض. (فتح، مستخلص)
In multiple locations: i.e., in two or three according to Muhammad. From Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one narration, it is not permissible unless there is a great river between the two locations, making them like two cities, and it is also a condition that there be no bridge over the river, or if there is, the imam orders the bridge to be cut off during the Friday prayer so that connection is severed. In another narration, he said: it is permissible if the city is large, in two locations, and not more than three. If they perform it in two locations, the Jumu'ah goes to whichever of them preceded, and the others must perform Zuhr if they are not sure which was first. If they performed it simultaneously or it is unknown, both are valid. Muhammad reports from Abu Hanifa that it is permissible in two or more locations. In al-Bahr, it is reported: I have given fatwa many times against praying it, for fear that the ignorant might believe that it is the obligation and that Jumu'ah is not the fard.

Validity of Jumu'ah in the Musalla and Status of Mina and Arafat
Ruling on Jumu'ah in the musalla and status of Mina and Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for Jumu'ah in the musalla and explain why Mina is considered a city during Hajj while Arafat is never a valid venue.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah is valid in the musalla as part of the city's courtyard, but Mina's city status is seasonal and Arafat is never a city.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a critical practical question: Where can Jumu'ah be validly performed? The text clarifies that the musalla (prayer ground) is legally annexed to the city, making Jumu'ah valid there. It then tackles the specific cases of Mina and Arafat during Hajj, highlighting an intra-Hanafi disagreement on Mina's status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on the musalla
The text states Jumu'ah is valid in the musalla (prayer ground) of a city, just as in the city itself.
The musalla is considered part of the city's courtyard (fina').
2
Understand the analogy (qiyas) to the city courtyard
The musalla is annexed to the city because it serves the needs of city dwellers (horses, armies, funerals, etc.). This is proven by qiyas: just as Jumu'ah is valid in the courtyard, it is valid in the musalla.
The illa is the functional annexation.
3
Note the extent of the musalla
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Imam Muhammad's estimation of one farsakh (approx. 3 miles) for the musalla's extent.
Al-Tahtawi mentions this as the chosen fatwa.
4
Analyze the dispute on Mina
Mina is considered a city during the Hajj season by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf due to buildings and streets. Imam Muhammad disagrees, holding it as a village. The mufta bihi follows the two (lahuma).
Jumu'ah in Mina requires the Caliph or Amir of Hijaz, not just the seasonal amir.
5
Understand Arafat's exclusion
Arafat is never a city; it is an open area (fina') and not part of Mecca's courtyard. Therefore Jumu'ah is never valid there, regardless of who is present.
The passage also clarifies linguistic points about the name 'Arafat'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو مصلاه، ومِناً مصر لا عرفات، وتُؤدّى في مصر في مواضع، المصر أي الجمعة أي واحد متعددة في موضعين فأكثر أو مصلاه: [وهو ما حوله لمصالحه مطلقاً، والمختار للفتوى تقديره بفرسخ. (ط)] الحكم غير مقصور على المصلى، بل تجوز الجمعة في جميع أفنية المصر؛ لأنها بمنزلة في حق حوائج أهل المصر من ركض الخيل وجمع العساكر وصلاة الجنازة ودفن الموتى ونحو ذلك، والمختار للفتوى قول محمد أنه مقدر بفرسخ، الحاصل: أنه تؤدى الجمعة في مصلى المصر مثل مصلى العيد سواء كان بينهما مزارع أولا ؛ لأنه يكون في فنائه، وفناؤه ملحق به، وكما أن المصر وفناؤه شرط جواز الجمعة، فهو شرط جواز صلاة العيد. (عيني، مسكين) ومناً مصر: [فتجوز إقامة الجمعة فيها إذا كان الإمام أمير الحجاز أو الخليفة لا أمير الموسم؛ لأنه يلي أمور الحج لا غير. (ط،ع)] وقال محمد: لا تجوز؛ لأنها من القرى ولهما أنها تتمصر في أيام الموسم، وفيها أبنية ودور وسكك، وهذا يشير إلى أنها لا تجوز في غير أيام الموسم؛ لأنها لا تبقى مصراً بعدها، وقيل: تجوز؛ لأنها مكة بناء على تقدير الفناء بفرسخين، لكن تقدير الفناء بذلك غير صحيح. (عيني، فتح) لا عرفات: [ أي هي ليست بمصر؛ لأنها فناء ولا من فناء مكة (ع)] ولو كان الخليفة بها في قولهم جميعاً، وهي علم للموقف ولكنها منصرف كمسلمات؛ لأن الألف والتاء تمنع تقدير تاء التأنيث فيها، والتي فيها ليست الألف علامة جمع المؤنث سميت بذلك؛ لأنها وصفت لإبراهيم عليه، فلما أبصرها عرفها، هي مع للتأنيث إنما وقيل: التقى فيها آدم وحواء عليهما السلام فتعارفا، وقيل: غير ذلك. (فتح)
Or his place of prayer, and Mina is a city, not Arafat, and it is performed in a city in places. The city: meaning the Friday prayer is in one city (but) multiple (places) in two or more locations. Or his place of prayer: [It is what surrounds it for its interests absolutely, and the chosen for fatwa is its estimation by a farsakh. (al-Tahtawi)] The ruling is not restricted to the musalla, rather Friday prayer is permissible in all courtyards of the city; because they are like it in terms of the needs of the city dwellers regarding galloping horses, gathering armies, funeral prayer, burial of the dead, and so on. And the chosen for fatwa is the statement of Muhammad that it is estimated by a farsakh. The gist: it is performed in the musalla of the city like the Eid musalla, whether there are farms between them or not; because it is in its courtyard, and its courtyard is annexed to it. And just as the city and its courtyard are a condition for the validity of Friday prayer, it is a condition for the validity of Eid prayer. (al-'Ayni, Miskeen) And Mina is a city: [Thus establishing Friday prayer in it is allowed if the imam is the Amir of Hijaz or the Caliph, not the Amir of the season; because he administers only Hajj affairs. (al-Tahtawi, al-'Ayni)] And Muhammad said: It is not allowed; because it is from the villages. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa?) said: It becomes a city during the season; there are buildings, houses, and streets. This indicates that it is not allowed outside the season; because it does not remain a city after it. And it was said: It is allowed; because it is (part of) Mecca based on estimating the courtyard as two farsakhs, but that estimation is not correct. (al-'Ayni, Fath) Not Arafat: [That is, it is not a city; because it is an open area and not from the courtyard of Mecca. (al-'Ayni)] Even if the Caliph is there according to all of them. And it is a proper noun for the standing place, but it is declined like 'Muslimat' because the alif and ta prevent the estimation of the ta of femininity, and it is with the ta for femininity. It was named so because it was described to Ibrahim, and when he saw it he recognized it. It was said that Adam and Eve met there and recognized each other. And other reasons. (al-Fath)
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the venue for Jumu'ah prayer. The ruling is that Jumu'ah is valid in the musalla (prayer ground) of a city, even if there are farms between, because the courtyard (fina') is annexed to the city. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the extent of the musalla is a farsakh (about 3 miles) according to Imam Muhammad. The text then addresses Mina and Arafat. Mina is considered a city during Hajj season due to its buildings and streets, so Jumu'ah is valid there if the ruling authority is the Caliph or the Amir of Hajj (not just the seasonal amir). Imam Muhammad holds that Mina is a village and Jumu'ah is not valid there. Arafat, in contrast, is not a city nor part of Mecca's courtyard, so Jumu'ah is never valid there regardless of who is present. The passage also clarifies linguistic points about the name 'Arafat.'

Key Terms
مصلى (musalla): The prayer ground or open space where Eid and Jumu'ah prayers are performed, considered part of the city's courtyard.
فرسخ (farsakh): A unit of distance approximately 3 miles; used here to estimate the extent of the musalla.
مصر (misr): A city with a ruler and congregation necessary for Jumu'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always
B) Yes, if the Caliph is present
C) No, never
D) Only during Hajj season

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah is valid in the musalla as part of the city's courtyard, but Mina's city status is seasonal and Arafat is never a valid venue.

Jumu'ah in Multiple Locations in a Single City
Intra-Hanafi dispute on multiple Jumu'ah locations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi Hanafi position on Jumu'ah in multiple locations and explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The relied-upon Hanafi position allows Jumu'ah in two locations within a city; more than two is invalid.

This lesson examines the Hanafi dispute on whether Jumu'ah can be held in more than one place in a single city. The passage presents the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and establishes the mufta bihi position. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for applying Jumu'ah in large urban environments today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi imams and their positions
List each imam's view on the number of allowed locations for Jumu'ah in one city: Abu Hanifa allows two or more; Abu Yusuf has two narrations; Muhammad allows two or three.
These are from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's two narrations
One narration restricts to two only if a great river separates them; the other allows two without a special condition. The more flexible narration is closer to Zahir al-Riwayah.
The river condition makes them like two separate cities.
3
Determine the Zahir al-Riwayah position
Zahir al-Riwayah, the most authoritative transmissions, states Jumu'ah is valid in two locations and no more. This is the mufta bihi.
The text says 'upon this is reliance'.
4
Understand the dalil: qiyas to Eid prayer
The proof is analogical reasoning from Eid prayer: 'Ali would go to the outskirts and appoint a deputy for the weak, showing two locations are permissible. Since Eid and Jumu'ah are both specific to the city, the same ruling applies.
The illa is 'being specific to the city' (ikhtisas bil-misr).
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
If three Jumu'ahs are held, the third must be repeated as Zuhr. If two are held, the earlier one is valid; if simultaneous, both are valid.
This practical consequence guides fatwa in large cities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في مواضع أي في موضعين أو ثلاثة عند محمد، وعن أبي يوسف روايتان في رواية لا يجوز إلا إذا كان بين موضعين نهر عظيم فيصير بمنزلة مصرين وقيل شرط أيضاً أن لا يكون على النهر جسر أو كان ولكن يأمر بقطع الجسر الجمعة حتى ينقطع الوصل، وفي رواية قال: يجوز إذا كان المصر عظيماً في موضعين، ولم يجز يوم في الثلاث، فإن أدوها في موضعين فالجمعة لمن سبق منهما وللآخرين أن يعيدوا الظهر، وإن أدوها معاً أو كان لا يدرى كيف كان يجوز صلاتهم، وروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجوز الجمعة في الموضعين أو أكثر وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز في موضعين ولا يجوز في أكثر من ذلك وعليه الاعتماد، فإنه روي أن علياً كان يخرج إلى الجبانة في العيد ويستخلف في المصر من يصلي بضعفة الناس وذلك بمحضر من الصحابة فلما جاز في صلاة العيد جاز في الجمعة؛ لأنهما في الاختصاص بالمصر يستويان. (فتح، مستخلص) تتمة: سئل السيد الحموي عن أربع ركعات التي بعد صلاة الجمعة وتسمى الظهر عندهم إذا اختلت بعض شروط الجمعة هل هي فرض أو واجبة أو مستحبة أو ليست بواحدة منها وما كيفية نية الظهر على القول بها؟ فأجاب بأنها ليست فرضا ولا واجبة ولا سنة، بل ولا أصل لها في المذهب، وقال في البحر: وقد أفتيت مراراً بعدم صلاتها خوفاً على اعتقاد الجهلة أنها الفرض وأن الجمعة ليست بفرض. (فتح، مستخلص)
In places, i.e., in two or three places according to Muhammad. And from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one narration it is not allowed unless there is a great river between them, making them like two cities; it was also said as a condition that there be no bridge over the river, or if there is, he orders the bridge to be cut on Friday to sever the connection. In another narration he said: It is allowed if the city is large in two places, and not allowed in three. If they perform it in two places, the Friday prayer is for the one which preceded, and for the others to repeat Zuhr. If they perform it simultaneously or it is unknown, both prayers are valid. And Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa that Jumu'ah is allowed in two or more places. And in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), it is allowed in two places and not allowed in more, and upon this is reliance. Because it is narrated that 'Ali used to go out to the cemetery for Eid and would deputize in the city someone to pray with the weak people, in the presence of the Companions. Since it was allowed for Eid prayer, it is allowed for Friday, because both are equal in being specific to the city. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Appendix: Al-Sayyid al-Hamawi was asked about the four rak'ahs after Friday prayer, called Zuhr among them, when some conditions of Friday are compromised: are they fard, wajib, mustahabb, or none, and what is the manner of the intention of Zuhr on that view? He answered that they are not fard, not wajib, not sunnah, rather they have no basis in the school. And in al-Bahr: I have given fatwa repeatedly against praying them, fearing that the ignorant might believe that they are the fard and that Friday is not fard. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq covers two separate topics. First, the ruling on holding Jumu'ah in multiple locations within the same city. There is significant ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams. The relied-upon position from Zahir al-Riwayah is that it is permissible in two locations but not more. If someone performs Jumu'ah in a third location, that prayer is not valid. The proof is qiyas to Eid prayer, where 'Ali (r) used to appoint a deputy in the city for the weak. Second, the appendix (tatmimah) addresses the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah that some people call 'Zuhr.' The correct Hanafi position is that these rak'ahs have no basis; they are not fard, wajib, or sunnah. Scholars like al-Hamawi and the author of al-Bahr discouraged them to prevent confusion that they might be substituted for Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The most authoritative transmissions of Imam Muhammad; here it refers to the position that Jumu'ah is allowed in two places.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), in how many locations can Jumu'ah be validly performed in one city?
A) Only one
B) Two
C) Three
D) Unlimited

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position allows Jumu'ah in two locations in one city; more than two is invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
5 min
The Four Rak'ahs After Jumu'ah (Tatimmah)
Appendix on post-Jumu'ah prayer ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi ruling on the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah and explain why they have no basis.

Core Idea
The four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah have no basis in the Hanafi school and should not be prayed.

This appendix (tatimmah) clarifies a common confusion: some people pray four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah, thinking it is a substitute if Jumu'ah is compromised. The Hanafi school firmly states that these rak'ahs have no foundation and are not fard, wajib, or sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question posed to al-Hamawi
The question concerns the legal status of the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah when some conditions of Jumu'ah are missing.
These rak'ahs are sometimes called 'Zuhr' among the Hanafis.
2
State al-Hamawi's answer
They are not fard, wajib, or sunnah; they have no basis in the madhhab.
The answer is definitive.
3
Understand the reasoning of al-Bahr
Al-Bahr gave fatwa against praying them, fearing that the ignorant might think they replace Jumu'ah.
This shows the harm in praying them.
4
Apply the ruling
Do not pray these four rak'ahs; regular sunnah prayers after Jumu'ah are not prescribed.
The Hanafi school does not have a specific sunnah after Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في مواضع أي في موضعين أو ثلاثة عند محمد، وعن أبي يوسف روايتان في رواية لا يجوز إلا إذا كان بين موضعين نهر عظيم فيصير بمنزلة مصرين وقيل شرط أيضاً أن لا يكون على النهر جسر أو كان ولكن يأمر بقطع الجسر الجمعة حتى ينقطع الوصل، وفي رواية قال: يجوز إذا كان المصر عظيماً في موضعين، ولم يجز يوم في الثلاث، فإن أدوها في موضعين فالجمعة لمن سبق منهما وللآخرين أن يعيدوا الظهر، وإن أدوها معاً أو كان لا يدرى كيف كان يجوز صلاتهم، وروى محمد عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجوز الجمعة في الموضعين أو أكثر وفي ظاهر الرواية يجوز في موضعين ولا يجوز في أكثر من ذلك وعليه الاعتماد، فإنه روي أن علياً كان يخرج إلى الجبانة في العيد ويستخلف في المصر من يصلي بضعفة الناس وذلك بمحضر من الصحابة فلما جاز في صلاة العيد جاز في الجمعة؛ لأنهما في الاختصاص بالمصر يستويان. (فتح، مستخلص) تتمة: سئل السيد الحموي عن أربع ركعات التي بعد صلاة الجمعة وتسمى الظهر عندهم إذا اختلت بعض شروط الجمعة هل هي فرض أو واجبة أو مستحبة أو ليست بواحدة منها وما كيفية نية الظهر على القول بها؟ فأجاب بأنها ليست فرضا ولا واجبة ولا سنة، بل ولا أصل لها في المذهب، وقال في البحر: وقد أفتيت مراراً بعدم صلاتها خوفاً على اعتقاد الجهلة أنها الفرض وأن الجمعة ليست بفرض. (فتح، مستخلص)
In places, i.e., in two or three places according to Muhammad. And from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one narration it is not allowed unless there is a great river between them, making them like two cities; it was also said as a condition that there be no bridge over the river, or if there is, he orders the bridge to be cut on Friday to sever the connection. In another narration he said: It is allowed if the city is large in two places, and not allowed in three. If they perform it in two places, the Friday prayer is for the one which preceded, and for the others to repeat Zuhr. If they perform it simultaneously or it is unknown, both prayers are valid. And Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa that Jumu'ah is allowed in two or more places. And in the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), it is allowed in two places and not allowed in more, and upon this is reliance. Because it is narrated that 'Ali used to go out to the cemetery for Eid and would deputize in the city someone to pray with the weak people, in the presence of the Companions. Since it was allowed for Eid prayer, it is allowed for Friday, because both are equal in being specific to the city. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Appendix: Al-Sayyid al-Hamawi was asked about the four rak'ahs after Friday prayer, called Zuhr among them, when some conditions of Friday are compromised: are they fard, wajib, mustahabb, or none, and what is the manner of the intention of Zuhr on that view? He answered that they are not fard, not wajib, not sunnah, rather they have no basis in the school. And in al-Bahr: I have given fatwa repeatedly against praying them, fearing that the ignorant might believe that they are the fard and that Friday is not fard. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq covers two separate topics. First, the ruling on holding Jumu'ah in multiple locations within the same city. There is significant ikhtilaf among Hanafi imams. The relied-upon position from Zahir al-Riwayah is that it is permissible in two locations but not more. If someone performs Jumu'ah in a third location, that prayer is not valid. The proof is qiyas to Eid prayer, where 'Ali (r) used to appoint a deputy in the city for the weak. Second, the appendix (tatmimah) addresses the four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah that some people call 'Zuhr.' The correct Hanafi position is that these rak'ahs have no basis; they are not fard, wajib, or sunnah. Scholars like al-Hamawi and the author of al-Bahr discouraged them to prevent confusion that they might be substituted for Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
تتمة (tatimmah): An additional appendix or supplement to the main discussion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They are a recommended sunnah
B) They are wajib if conditions are missing
C) They have no basis and are not fard, wajib, or sunnah
D) They are permissible but not recommended

Key Takeaway
The four rak'ahs after Jumu'ah have no basis in the Hanafi school and should not be prayed.

Salah — Prayer

Conditions for Jumu'ah: The Ruler and the Time
Ruling that Jumu'ah requires a ruler or deputy and must be within Zuhr time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for Jumu'ah (presence of a ruler or deputy and performance within Zuhr time) and evaluate the inter-madhhab disputes regarding each condition.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires a ruler to prevent disputes and must be within Zuhr time; otherwise it reverts to Zuhr.

This lesson dissects two essential conditions for Jumu'ah prayer according to the Hanafi school. The first is the presence of a ruling authority (sultan or his deputy) to maintain order in the large congregation; the second is the timing strictly within the Zuhr period. The Hanafi proofs are drawn from hadith, the statement of al-Hasan al-Basri, and rational arguments. We will also examine the Shafi'i position that dispenses with the ruler condition and the differing views on time expiration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the opening phrase: 'والسلطان أو نائبه ووقت الظهر'. These are two shurut (conditions) for the validity of Jumu'ah: the presence of a ruler or his deputy, and the time of Zuhr.
The condition applies even if the ruler is a usurper, as long as his conduct is that of a ruler.
2
Examine the proof for the ruler condition
The Hanafi proof is the hadith: 'من تركها استخفافاً بها وله إمام عادل أو جائر فلا جمع الله شمله' (Whoever abandons it out of contempt while he has an imam...), and the statement of al-Hasan al-Basri that Friday is one of four things entrusted to the sultan. The rational argument: large gatherings cause disputes; the ruler settles them.
The hadith implies the necessity of an imam (ruler) for Jumu'ah.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Shafi'i cites the hadith that 'Ali led Jumu'ah during the siege of 'Uthman without a ruler. Hanafi responds that 'Ali likely had 'Uthman's permission. Also, other fard prayers do not require a ruler, but Jumu'ah needs congregation and order.
The Hanafi position is that Jumu'ah is not like other fard prayers because of its public nature.
4
Understand the time condition and disputes
The proof for Zuhr time is the hadith when the Prophet sent Mus'ab: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Friday prayer.' If the time of Zuhr exits before the prayer is completed (before sitting for tashahhud), Jumu'ah is invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr. Shafi'i says complete as four rak'ahs because Friday is shortened Zuhr; Malik says time extends to sunset.
Hanafi holds Jumu'ah is an independent prayer, not shortened Zuhr.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, in the Hanafi school, Jumu'ah cannot be held without any ruler (even a non-Muslim authority may be substituted if they allow order). In Shafi'i, any Muslim community can hold Jumu'ah. Regarding time, if missed, Hanafi prays Zuhr; Shafi'i completes as four; Malik continues with Jumu'ah.
These differences affect how communities organize Jumu'ah under various political circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ع، ط)] أي مطلقاً سواء قلد السلطنة . الخليفة، أو كان متغلباً، وقال الشافعي الله السلطان والنائب ليسا بشرط؛ لما روي أن عليا منه صلى بالناس الجمعة حين كان عثمان محصوراً؛ ولأنها فرض فلا يشترط لها السلطان كسائر الفرائض، ولنا قوله عليه: "من تركها استخفافاً بها وله إمام عادل أو جائر فلا جمع الله شمله" الحديث، شرط أن يكون له إمام، وقال الحسن البصري: أربع إلى السلطان وذكر منها الجمعة، ومثله لا يعرف إلا سماعاً، فيحمل عليه، ولأنها تؤدى بجمع عظيم، فتقع المنازعة في التقديم أو في الأداء في أول الوقت فيليها السلطان تسكيناً للفتنة والمنازعة، وحديث علي الله يحتمل أنه فعله بإذن عثمان الله فلا يلزم حجة مع الاحتمال تبيين الحقائق: ٥٢٧/١] (فتح) ووقت الظهر : أي شرط لأدائها وقت الظهر، ولا تقدم على زوال الشمس؛ لما روي أن النبي عليه لما بعث مصعب بن عمير ههه إلى المدينة، قال له: "إذا زالت الشمس فصل بالناس الجمعة ؛ ولأنه عليها كان يصليها بعد الزوال، وعند أحمد تجوز قبله وقوله: "تبطل" "بخروجه أي إذا لم يؤدوها حتى خرج وقت الظهر ودخل وقت العصر سقط الجمعة وكذا لو خرج الوقت وهو فيها قبل ما قعد قدر التشهد يستقبل الظهر اتفاقاً، وقال الشافعي: أتمهما أربعاً؛ لأن الجمعة ظهر مقصور لأجل الخطبة؛ لقول عمر الله إنما قصرت الصلاة لمكان الخطبة، لكن قصرها مشروط بالوقت، فإذا فات عادت أربعاً؛ لأن الجمعة ليست فرضاً مستقلاً عنده، بل هي في الأصل ظهر ثم قصرت وعند مالك: بمضي على الجمعة؛ لأن وقتها يمتد إلى الغروب أي الوقت الضروري (مستخلص، فتح) بخروجه: أي بخروج وقت الظهر وهو فيها ولا يبني عليها؛ لاختلاف الصلاتين خلافاً لمالك والشافعي. (ط، ع)
And the sultan or his deputy, and the time of Zuhr, so it becomes invalid with its exit, and the khutbah before it, and two khutbahs are recommended. The one ordered to establish it even if a slave. Condition for its performance also, i.e., Friday. Meaning condition for its performance also: the sultan or his deputy, even if the sultan is a usurper without decree from the caliph if his conduct is that of the princes. (al-'Ayni, al-Tahtawi) Meaning absolutely, whether he has been appointed caliph or is a usurper. And al-Shafi'i said the sultan and his deputy are not a condition; because it is narrated that 'Ali led the people in Friday prayer when 'Uthman was besieged; and because it is a fard, so the sultan is not required like other fard prayers. Our proof is his statement: 'Whoever abandons it out of contempt, while he has a just or unjust imam, may Allah not gather his affairs together' — the hadith, stipulating that he has an imam. And al-Hasan al-Basri said: Four things are for the sultan, including Friday, and such a statement is only known through hearing, so it is relied upon. And because it is performed with a large gathering, so disputes arise over precedence or performance at the beginning of time, so the sultan undertakes it to calm fitna and dispute. And the hadith of 'Ali is likely that he did it with 'Uthman's permission, so it is not a proof with probability. (al-Fath) And the time of Zuhr: meaning a condition for its performance is the time of Zuhr, and it is not valid before zawal because it is narrated that the Prophet sent Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr to Medina, he said: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Friday prayer.' And because he used to pray it after zawal. And according to Ahmad, it is valid before it. And his saying: 'It becomes invalid' 'with its exit' means if they do not perform it until the time of Zuhr leaves and the time of 'Asr enters, Friday prayer is invalid. Similarly, if the time leaves while he is in it before he has sat for the amount of tashahhud, he must start Zuhr, by agreement. And al-Shafi'i said: He completes it as four; because Friday is Zuhr shortened for the sake of the khutbah, based on 'Umar's statement: 'The prayer was shortened because of the khutbah.' But its shortening is conditional on time, so if it is missed, it returns to four; because Friday is not an independent fard according to him, rather it is originally Zuhr then shortened. And according to Malik: He continues with Friday prayer; because its time extends to sunset, i.e., the necessary time. (Mustakhlas, al-Fath) 'With its exit': i.e., with the exit of the time of Zuhr while he is in it, and he does not build upon it; because the two prayers are different, contrary to Malik and al-Shafi'i. (al-Tahtawi, al-'Ayni)
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains two essential conditions for Jumu'ah. First, the presence of a ruler (sultan) or his deputy, even if the ruler came to power by force (mutaghallib). The Hanafi school requires this, unlike the Shafi'i school. The proof is the hadith about having an imam for Friday, and the rational argument that the ruler prevents disputes in large gatherings. Second, Jumu'ah must be performed within the time of Zuhr (from zawal until the time of 'Asr). If the time expires before completing the prayer, or even during it before sitting for tashahhud, Jumu'ah is invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr. There are disputes with Ahmad (allows before zawal), Shafi'i (completes as four if time goes out), and Malik (extends time to sunset). The Hanafi position is clear: Jumu'ah is a separate prayer, so it cannot be built upon for Zuhr.

Key Terms
سلطان (sultan): The ruling authority (caliph or usurper) who establishes public order; his presence is required for Jumu'ah.
وقت الظهر (waqt al-zuhr): The period from zawal (sun's decline) until the time of 'Asr; the only time Jumu'ah can be offered.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if Jumu'ah prayer is not completed before the time of 'Asr enters?
A) Complete as four rak'ahs of Jumu'ah
B) Repeat as Zuhr prayer
C) Continue and it becomes 'Asr
D) It is valid even if late

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah requires the presence of a ruler (or deputy) and must be performed strictly within the time of Zuhr; otherwise it is invalid and must be replaced by Zuhr.

The Jumu'ah Khutbah: Conditions and the Sunnah of Two Sermons
Ruling that the khutbah must precede Jumu'ah and is sunnah to be two

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for a valid Jumu'ah khutbah and explain why two khutbahs are sunnah (not wajib) according to the Hanafi school, using the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah as proof.

Core Idea
The khutbah is a condition for Jumu'ah, but two sermons are only recommended—one suffices for validity.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on the Jumu'ah khutbah. You will learn the essential conditions for a valid khutbah, the recommended (sunnah) practices, and the proof that two khutbahs are not mandatory. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with commentary from al-Nahr al-Fa'iq, establishes these rules with clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the khutbah as a condition (shart)
Recognize that the khutbah must precede the Jumu'ah prayer. It is not a rukn but a condition, meaning without it the prayer is invalid.
In Hanafi fiqh, conditions are external to the act but necessary for validity.
2
List the three conditions of the khutbah
The khutbah must be after zawal (midday), must be in the presence of a congregation with whom Jumu'ah is valid, and must be before the prayer. If any is missing, the khutbah is invalid.
The congregation can be deaf or sleeping; presence is required, not attentiveness.
3
Identify the sunnah (recommended) practices
Among the sunnah acts: two khutbahs (with a brief sitting between), raising the voice, being louder in the second, mentioning the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and keeping the khutbah short (about one surah).
These are commendable but not obligatory.
4
Examine the dalil (proof) from hadith
The hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah states that the Prophet initially delivered one khutbah, but later made them two with a sitting between. This indicates that one is sufficient and the sitting is for rest, not a condition.
The Hanafi school uses this hadith to argue that two khutbahs are sunnah, not wajib.
5
Apply the ruling: validity vs. completeness
If a single khutbah is delivered, Jumu'ah is valid but it is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) because the sunnah is abandoned. If all conditions are met, the prayer is valid.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the scope of obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخطبة قبلها لأن شرط الشيء سابق عليه، ويشترط أن تكون بعد الزوال، وأن تكون بحضرة جماعة تنعقد الجمعة بهم وإن كانوا صماً أو نياماً، ولو خطب وحده لا تجوز الخطبة، ومن المستحب أن يرفع الخطيب صوته، وأن يكون الجهر في الثانية دون الأولى، وذكر الخلفاء الراشدين مستحسن، والدعاء للسلطان بالنصر لا يستحب بل يكره، وقال عطاء: إنه محدث، وإنما كانت الخطبة تذكيراً، والدنو من الإمام أفضل من التباعد، وما يفعله المؤذنون حال الخطبة من الصلاة على النبي والترضي عن الصحابة فمكروه اتفاقاً، وتسن خطبتان؛ لحديث جابر بن سمرة أنه كان يخطب قائماً خطبة واحدة، فلما أسن جعلها خطبتين يجلس بينهما جلسة، ففي هذا دليل على أنه يجوز الاكتفاء بالخطبة، وعلى أن الجلسة بينهما للاستراحة لا للشرط (فتح) قبلها حتى لو صلوا بلا خطبة أو صلوا قبل الخطبة أو خطب قبل الوقت لم تجز. (ط) خطبتان خفيفتان قدر سورة من طوال المفصل. [النهر الفائق: ٣٥٨/١]
And the khutbah before it, because the condition of something precedes it. It is required that it be after zawal, and that it be in the presence of a congregation with whom Jumu'ah is valid even if they are deaf or sleeping. If he preaches alone, the khutbah is not valid. Among the recommended acts are that the preacher raise his voice, and that he be loud in the second khutbah but not the first. Mentioning the Rightly Guided Caliphs is commendable. Praying for the sultan's victory is not recommended but is disliked. 'Ata said: It is an innovation. The khutbah was only a reminder. Being close to the imam is better than being far. What the mu'adhdhins do during the khutbah of sending blessings upon the Prophet and being pleased with the Companions is unanimously disliked. And two khutbahs are recommended; due to the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah that he (the Prophet) used to deliver one khutbah standing, but when he grew older, he made them two, sitting between them. This indicates that one khutbah suffices, and that the sitting between them is for rest, not a condition. (al-Fath) Before it, so if they pray without a khutbah, or pray before the khutbah, or deliver the khutbah before the time, it is not valid. (al-Tahtawi) Two light khutbahs of about a surah from the long mufassal. [al-Nahr al-Fa'iq: 1/358]
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the khutbah for Jumu'ah. The khutbah must precede the prayer, be after zawal, and be delivered in the presence of a congregation (even if deaf or asleep). If the imam preaches alone without listeners, it is invalid. The sunnah (recommended) practices include raising the voice, being loud in the second khutbah, mentioning the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and sitting briefly between two khutbahs. Praying for the sultan is disliked, and the mu'adhdhins' blessings during the khutbah are unanimously disliked. The hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah is proof that two khutbahs are recommended, but one is sufficient. The sitting between is for rest, not a condition. The khutbahs themselves should be short, about the length of a surah from the long mufassal (e.g., Surah al-Hujurat to al-Buruj).

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam before Jumu'ah prayer; a condition for validity.
خطبتان (khutbatan): Two sermons separated by a brief sitting; sunnah according to Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is Jumu'ah valid if only one khutbah is delivered?
A) No, it is invalid
B) Yes, but it is not recommended
C) Yes, and it is recommended
D) No, unless there is a valid excuse

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that one khutbah suffices for Jumu'ah, but two are sunnah; the conditions of time and congregation are essential.

The Sultan as a Condition for Jumu'ah: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains requirement of sultan or deputy for Jumu'ah with proof and refutation of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition of the sultan for Jumu'ah, state the Shafi'i counterargument, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah requires a ruler to prevent fitna – even a usurper suffices if he acts like a ruler.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether the presence of the sultan is a condition for the validity of Jumu'ah. The Hanafi school maintains that a ruler or his deputy is required, drawing on hadith and the need for order in large congregations. The Shafi'i school disagrees, citing the example of Ali during Uthman's siege. Understanding this ikhtilaf illuminates how each school weights textual and rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the sultan or his deputy is a condition for Jumu'ah. Even a usurper suffices if his conduct resembles that of rulers.
The condition is for validity, not obligation.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the sultan is not a condition. Jumu'ah is an obligation like any other, so no special authority is required.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school cites the action of Ali (ra) leading Jumu'ah during Uthman's siege without formal appointment. They also argue by qiyas: if other obligations don't require a ruler, Jumu'ah shouldn't either.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: Ali's action was likely with Uthman's permission, so it does not negate the condition. The hadith explicitly requires an imam. Rationale: large gatherings need a leader to avoid strife.
Hanafis also cite Hasan al-Basri's statement, which they treat as a transmitted proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: According to Hanafi, Jumu'ah without a ruler is invalid. According to Shafi'i, it is valid. This affects communities without an Islamic ruler.
Hanafi mufta bihi: even a usurper suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسلطان أو نائبه بالرفع عطف على قوله: "بالمصر" يعني شرط أدائها أيضاً السلطان أو نائبه ولو كان السلطان متغلباً لا منشور له من الخليفة إذا كانت سيرته سيرة الأمراء. (ع، ط)] أي مطلقاً سواء قلد السلطنة . الخليفة، أو كان متغلباً، وقال الشافعي الله السلطان والنائب ليسا بشرط؛ لما روي أن عليا منه صلى بالناس الجمعة حين كان عثمان محصوراً؛ ولأنها فرض فلا يشترط لها السلطان كسائر الفرائض، ولنا قوله عليه: "من تركها استخفافاً بها وله إمام عادل أو جائر فلا جمع الله شمله" الحديث، شرط أن يكون له إمام، وقال الحسن البصري: أربع إلى السلطان وذكر منها الجمعة، ومثله لا يعرف إلا سماعاً، فيحمل عليه، ولأنها تؤدى بجمع عظيم، فتقع المنازعة في التقديم أو في الأداء في أول الوقت فيليها السلطان تسكيناً للفتنة والمنازعة، وحديث علي الله يحتمل أنه فعله بإذن عثمان الله فلا يلزم حجة مع الاحتمال تبيين الحقائق: ٥٢٧/١] (فتح)
And the sultan or his deputy (in nominative case, coordinated with 'in the city' meaning a condition for its performance is also the sultan or his deputy, even if the sultan is a usurper without a mandate from the caliph if his conduct is like that of rulers. (A, T) i.e., absolutely whether he was appointed by the caliph or a usurper. Al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) said: The sultan and his deputy are not conditions; because it is narrated that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) led the people in Jumu'ah when Uthman was besieged; and because it is an obligation, so the sultan is not required for it like other obligations. And our proof is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever abandons it out of disdain while having a just or unjust imam, may Allah not unite his affairs' - the hadith stipulated having an imam. And Hasan al-Basri said: Four things are with the sultan, and he mentioned Jumu'ah among them. Such a statement is not known except through hearing, so it is taken. And because it is performed with a large congregation, so dispute may arise about precedence or performance at the beginning of the time, so the sultan undertakes it to calm fitna and dispute. The hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) is likely that he did so with Uthman's permission, so it does not serve as proof due to probability. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 1/527) (Fath)
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the condition of the ruler for Jumu'ah. The Hanafi position, as stated by Imam Abu Hanifa, is that Jumu'ah requires the presence of the sultan (ruler) or his deputy. This is taken from the statement of Hasan al-Basri that four things are entrusted to the ruler, including Jumu'ah. The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever abandons it out of disdain while having an imam...' and the rational argument that large gatherings need a leader to prevent disputes. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, citing that Ali led Jumu'ah during Uthman's siege without a formal appointment, and arguing that like other obligations, Jumu'ah does not require a ruler. The Hanafi response is that Ali's action was likely with Uthman's permission, and the hadith explicitly requires an imam. The commentary notes that even a usurping ruler (mutaghallib) suffices if his conduct is like that of rulers. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): The ruler in authority, including a usurper if his conduct resembles that of rulers.
النائب (al-na'ib): Deputy of the sultan appointed to lead Jumu'ah.
متغلب (mutaghallib): A usurper who seizes power without formal appointment from the caliph.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding a usurper (mutaghallib) as the sultan for Jumu'ah?
A) He is not accepted because he did not receive a mandate from the caliph.
B) He is accepted only if he is just.
C) He is accepted if his conduct resembles that of rulers.
D) He is never accepted for Jumu'ah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a de facto ruler or his deputy for the validity of Jumu'ah, even if that ruler is a usurper, based on hadith and the need to prevent fitna.

Time Condition for Jumu'ah and Ruling When Time Exits
Explains that Jumu'ah time is Zuhr, cannot precede zawal, and ruling if time exits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi condition that Jumu'ah time must be after zawal and state the ruling if Zuhr time exits, distinguishing between the positions of Ahmad, Shafi'i, and Malik.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah time is Zuhr time; if it exits, Jumu'ah is invalid and must be made up as Zuhr.

This lesson examines a key condition for Jumu'ah: it must be performed within the time of Zuhr, after the sun's declination (zawal). We then explore what happens if the congregation delays Jumu'ah until Zuhr time ends. The Hanafi school holds that Jumu'ah becomes invalid and must be repeated as Zuhr, but other schools disagree. Understanding this dispute clarifies the relationship between Jumu'ah and Zuhr and the importance of timely performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
What is the condition for Jumu'ah according to all schools? It must be performed within a specific time—the time of Zuhr after zawal.
The condition of time is a shart for validity.
2
State the Hanafi position on the start time
Hanafi: Jumu'ah cannot be performed before zawal; it must be after. Two proofs: the hadith of Mus'ab and the Prophet's practice.
The hadith: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah.'
3
State the Hanafi position on the end time
If Zuhr time exits while the congregation is still praying Jumu'ah (before they have sat for tashahhud), Jumu'ah becomes batil (invalid) and they must pray Zuhr (4 rak'ahs) anew.
This is because Jumu'ah and Zuhr are different prayers.
4
Detail the opposing positions
Ahmad allows before zawal; Shafi'i says complete as 4 rak'ahs of Zuhr; Malik says continue Jumu'ah because its time extends to sunset.
Each school bases its view on different proofs.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response emphasizes that the hadith specifies after zawal, and Jumu'ah and Zuhr are distinct prayers with different niyyah, so one cannot build upon the other.
Thus, if time exits, a fresh Zuhr is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووقت الظهر : أي شرط لأدائها وقت الظهر، ولا تقدم على زوال الشمس؛ لما روي أن النبي عليه لما بعث مصعب بن عمير ههه إلى المدينة، قال له: "إذا زالت الشمس فصل بالناس الجمعة ؛ ولأنه عليها كان يصليها بعد الزوال، وعند أحمد تجوز قبله وقوله: "تبطل" "بخروجه أي إذا لم يؤدوها حتى خرج وقت الظهر ودخل وقت العصر سقط الجمعة وكذا لو خرج الوقت وهو فيها قبل ما قعد قدر التشهد يستقبل الظهر اتفاقاً، وقال الشافعي: أتمهما أربعاً؛ لأن الجمعة ظهر مقصور لأجل الخطبة؛ لقول عمر الله إنما قصرت الصلاة لمكان الخطبة، لكن قصرها مشروط بالوقت، فإذا فات عادت أربعاً؛ لأن الجمعة ليست فرضاً مستقلاً عنده، بل هي في الأصل ظهر ثم قصرت وعند مالك: بمضي على الجمعة؛ لأن وقتها يمتد إلى الغروب أي الوقت الضروري (مستخلص، فتح) بخروجه: أي بخروج وقت الظهر وهو فيها ولا يبني عليها؛ لاختلاف الصلاتين خلافاً لمالك والشافعي. (ط، ع)
And the time of Zuhr: i.e., a condition for its performance is the time of Zuhr. It is not valid before the sun's declination; because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he sent Mus'ab ibn 'Umayr to Medina, said to him: 'When the sun declines, lead the people in Jumu'ah.' And because he used to pray it after declination. According to Ahmad, it is permissible before. And his statement: 'It becomes invalid by its exit' means if they do not perform it until the time of Zuhr exits and the time of 'Asr enters, Jumu'ah is nullified. Similarly, if the time exits while they are in it before they have sat for the amount of tashahhud, they must start Zuhr anew by agreement. Al-Shafi'i said: They complete it as four rak'ahs because Jumu'ah is Zuhr shortened for the sake of the khutbah, based on 'Umar's statement: 'The prayer was shortened because of the khutbah.' But its shortening is conditional upon time, so if time is lost, it returns to four rak'ahs because Jumu'ah is not an independent obligation in his view; rather it is originally Zuhr then shortened. According to Malik: They continue with Jumu'ah because its time extends to sunset i.e., the necessary time. (Mukhtasar, Fath) 'By its exit': i.e., if the time of Zuhr exits while they are in it, they do not build upon it due to the difference of the two prayers, contrary to Malik and al-Shafi'i. (T, A)
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage covers the condition of time for Jumu'ah and the disagreement about what happens when the time of Zuhr expires. The Hanafi position is that Jumu'ah must be performed after zawal (declination of the sun) within Zuhr time. If the time exits before the congregation has sat for the tashahhud, Jumu'ah becomes invalid and they must pray Zuhr (four rak'ahs) anew. This is based on the practice of the Prophet and the narration to Mus'ab. Imam Ahmad allows Jumu'ah before zawal. Imam al-Shafi'i considers Jumu'ah as shortened Zuhr; if time exits, he says to complete it as four rak'ahs of Zuhr because the shortening was conditional upon time. Imam Malik says they continue with Jumu'ah because its time extends until sunset. The Hanafi response is that Jumu'ah and Zuhr are different prayers (different niyyah), so one cannot build upon the other.

Key Terms
الوقت (al-waqt): The time of Zuhr prayer, starting from zawal until the shadow of an object reaches twice its length (in Hanafi).
الزوال (al-zawal): The sun's declination from the meridian; the beginning of Zuhr time.
تبطل (tabtul): Here, Jumu'ah becomes invalid (batil) if time exits before completing the sitting for tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must the congregation do if the time of Zuhr exits while they are still praying Jumu'ah and they have not yet sat for tashahhud?
A) Complete Jumu'ah as two rak'ahs.
B) Complete Jumu'ah as four rak'ahs.
C) Abandon Jumu'ah and pray Zuhr four rak'ahs anew.
D) Continue Jumu'ah because time extends to sunset.

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah must be performed within Zuhr time after zawal; if time exits before sitting for tashahhud, it is invalid and must be made up as Zuhr.
