Conditions and Etiquettes of the Jumu'ah Khutbah
Lists conditions and etiquettes of the Jumu'ah khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the validity of the Jumu'ah khutbah and distinguish between mustahabb and makruh actions during it.

Core Idea
The khutbah must be before the prayer, after zawal, and with a valid congregation.

The Jumu'ah khutbah is a condition for the validity of the Jumu'ah prayer. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq outlines the essential conditions and also highlights recommended and disliked practices. Understanding these helps ensure our Jumu'ah is performed correctly and respectfully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
The text begins by stating that the khutbah must be before the prayer, because a condition precedes the conditioned. Note this logical relationship.
2
Identify the second condition
The khutbah must be after zawal (the time when the sun declines from its zenith). This is the time of Zuhr.
3
Identify the third condition
The khutbah must be in the presence of a congregation that would make Jumu'ah valid. Even if they are deaf or asleep, but if the khatib delivers it alone, it is invalid.
4
Distinguish mustahabb from makruh
The text lists recommended acts (raising voice, second khutbah louder, mentioning caliphs) and disliked acts (praying for sultan's victory, mu'adhdhins sending blessings during khutbah). Categorize each.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخطبة قبلها لأن شرط الشيء سابق عليه، ويشترط أن تكون بعد الزوال، وأن تكون بحضرة جماعة تنعقد الجمعة بهم وإن كانوا صماً أو نياماً، ولو خطب وحده لا تجوز الخطبة، ومن المستحب أن يرفع الخطيب صوته، وأن يكون الجهر في الثانية دون الأولى، وذكر الخلفاء الراشدين مستحسن، والدعاء للسلطان بالنصر لا يستحب بل يكره، وقال عطاء: إنه محدث، وإنما كانت الخطبة تذكيراً، والدنو من الإمام أفضل من التباعد، وما يفعله المؤذنون حال الخطبة من الصلاة على النبي والترضي عن الصحابة فمكروه اتفاقاً
And the khutbah before it, because a condition precedes its conditioned. It is required that it be after zawal, and that it be in the presence of a congregation with which Jumu'ah is valid, even if they are deaf or asleep. If one delivers the khutbah alone, the khutbah is not valid. It is mustahabb for the khatib to raise his voice, and that the jahr (loudness) be in the second khutbah rather than the first. Mention of the Rightly Guided Caliphs is mustahasan (good). Supplication for the sultan for victory is not mustahabb but rather makruh. 'Ata said: It is an innovation; rather the khutbah was a reminder. Being close to the imam is better than being far. What the mu'adhdhins do during the khutbah of sending blessings on the Prophet and being pleased with the Companions is makruh by agreement.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage states the conditions and recommended practices for the khutbah of Jumu'ah. First, the khutbah must be before the prayer because a condition precedes the conditioned. Second, it must be after zawal (the time of Zuhr). Third, it must be in the presence of a congregation that would make Jumu'ah valid, even if those present are deaf or asleep. If the imam delivers the khutbah alone, it is not valid. Several sunnah and makruh aspects are mentioned: raising the voice, making the second khutbah louder, mentioning the caliphs is good, but praying for the ruler's victory is makruh according to 'Ata's view that it is an innovation. The mu'adhdhins sending blessings on the Prophet during the khutbah is also makruh by agreement. This passage is a straightforward ruling statement without extensive proof or dispute.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered before Jumu'ah prayer; a condition for its validity.
المستحب (al-mustahabb): Recommended actions: raising voice, jahr in second khutbah, mentioning caliphs.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked acts: dua for sultan's victory, mu'adhdhins sending blessings during khutbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Raising the voice.
B) Mentioning the Rightly Guided Caliphs.
C) Praying for the sultan's victory.
D) Sitting close to the imam.

Key Takeaway
The Jumu'ah khutbah must be before the prayer, after zawal, and with a congregation; certain actions are recommended, others disliked.

Sunnah of Two Khutbahs and Their Conditions
Explains the sunnah of two khutbahs, their minimal content, and required conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of Jumu'ah khutbahs, identify the minimal valid content, and list the conditions for a valid khutbah.

Core Idea
Two khutbahs are sunnah; one suffices and a single praise is enough.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on Jumu'ah khutbahs. Many assume two khutbahs are obligatory, but the Hanafi school holds them as sunnah muakkadah. The proof comes from the practice of the Prophet as reported by Jabir ibn Samurah. The text also details the minimal content and conditions, such as purity, standing, and the sitting between the khutbahs being for rest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Note that the text begins with 'تسن خطبتان' – two khutbahs are sunnah. Understand the Hanafi hierarchy: sunnah muakkadah means recommended but not obligatory.
Contrast with Shafi'i who consider them fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah. The Prophet initially gave one khutbah, then later gave two with a sitting. This shows the permissibility of one and the recommendation of two.
The sitting is described as for rest, not a condition.
3
List the conditions
The text specifies conditions: the khutbah must be after zawal and before prayer, the khatib must be in a state of purity and standing, and minimal content is a single praise (tahmidah, tahlilah, or tasbihah).
The sitting between them is also recommended but not a condition.
4
Identify invalidators
The text states that praying without a khutbah, praying before the khutbah, or delivering the khutbah before the time invalidates the prayer.
This shows the khutbah is an essential part of Jumu'ah, but not a pillar in the strict sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتسن خطبتان؛ لحديث جابر بن سمرة أنه كان يخطب قائماً خطبة واحدة، فلما أسن جعلها خطبتين يجلس بينهما جلسة، ففي هذا دليل على أنه يجوز الاكتفاء بالخطبة، وعلى أن الجلسة بينهما للاستراحة لا للشرط (فتح) قبلها حتى لو صلوا بلا خطبة أو صلوا قبل الخطبة أو خطب قبل الوقت لم تجز. (ط) خطبتان خفيفتان قدر سورة من طوال المفصل. [النهر الفائق: ٣٥٨/١] بجلسة بينهما بطهارة قائما وكفت تحميدة أو تهليلة أو تسبيحة، والجماعة وهم ثلاثة
أي في الخطبة أي قوله الحمد لله أي قوله لا إله إلا الله
بينهما أي بين الخطبتين ومقدارها أن يستقر كل عضو منه في موضعه يحمد في الأولى، ويصلي على النبي،
ويعظ الناس، وفي الثانية كذلك، إلا أنه يدعو مكان الوعظ كذا جرى التوارث [رمز الحقائق: ۹۸/۱]
And two khutbahs are recommended (sunnah); due to the hadith of Jabir ibn Samurah that he would deliver one khutbah standing, then when he grew older he made them two khutbahs with a sitting between them. This indicates that one khutbah is permissible, and that the sitting between them is for rest, not a condition. (Fath) Before it, so if they prayed without a khutbah, or prayed before the khutbah, or delivered the khutbah before the time, it is not valid. (T) Two short khutbahs, about the length of a surah from the long mufassal. [Al-Nahr al-Fa'iq 1/358] With a sitting between them, in a state of purity, standing, and a single tahmidah, tahlilah, or tasbihah suffices. And the congregation is three... (then commentary on the khutbah) i.e., in the khutbah, i.e., saying 'Alhamdulillah', i.e., saying 'La ilaha illallah'. Between them, i.e., between the two khutbahs, and its amount is that each limb settles in its place. In the first, he praises Allah, sends blessings on the Prophet, and exhorts the people. In the second similarly, except that he makes supplication instead of exhortation. This has been inherited. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/98]
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of two khutbahs for Jumu'ah. They are sunnah (recommended), not obligatory. The proof is from the practice of the Prophet as reported by Jabir ibn Samurah. Initially he would give one khutbah, but later he gave two with a sitting in between. This shows that one khutbah is sufficient but two are better. The sitting between them is for rest, not a condition. Conditions for the khutbah include that it must be after zawal and before the prayer. The khutbahs should be short. Additional requirements include: a sitting between the two khutbahs, purity of the khatib, standing, and the minimal content being a single phrase praising Allah (like 'Alhamdulillah', 'La ilaha illallah', or 'Subhanallah'). In the first khutbah, the khatib praises Allah, sends blessings on the Prophet, and exhorts the people. In the second, he does similarly except that he makes supplication instead of exhortation.

Key Terms
تسن (tusannu): It is sunnah (recommended) to perform two khutbahs.
تحميدة (tahmidah): Saying 'Alhamdulillah' (Praise be to Allah); minimal valid content of khutbah.
جلسة (jalsah): The sitting between the two khutbahs; recommended but not a condition.
تسبيحة (tasbihah): Saying 'Subhanallah' (Glory be to Allah); another minimal valid content.
تهليلة (tahlilah): Saying 'La ilaha illallah' (There is no god but Allah); another minimal valid content.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum content of a valid khutbah according to the Hanafi school as stated in the text?
A) At least two verses from Quran.
B) A single tahmidah, tahlilah, or tasbihah.
C) The entire Surah Al-Fatiha.
D) A lengthy sermon with blessings on the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Two khutbahs for Jumu'ah are sunnah in the Hanafi school; a single phrase of praise suffices, and the sitting between them is for rest, not a condition.

Minimum Congregation for Jumu'ah: Three or Two Besides the Imam
Inter-madhhab dispute on Jumu'ah congregation number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on minimum Jumu'ah congregation, evaluate their proofs, and identify the mufta bihi within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
For Jumu'ah, the Hanafi school counts the imam separately; the minimum congregation is either three (Abu Hanifa) or two (Abu Yusuf) besides him.

This lesson examines a key condition for the validity of Jumu'ah: the number of participants. The Hanafi school holds that a small number suffices, while the Shafi'i school requires forty. We will explore the Quranic and hadith evidence and see how the Hanafi scholars differed among themselves, concluding with the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof from the Quran
Identify that the Hanafi school requires a congregation besides the imam. Abu Hanifa requires three, Abu Yusuf requires two. The proof is from Quran 62:9 where the plural 'hasten' (اسعوا) indicates at least two, plus the caller makes three.
The text also cites 62:11 where twelve men remained with the Prophet, indicating sufficiency.
2
State the opposing (Shafi'i) position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i requires forty free resident men besides the imam. His proofs include the hadith of Jabir (sunnah that every three have an imam, and for forty there is Jumu'ah) and the hadith of Abd al-Rahman ibn Malik (first Jumu'ah had forty men).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence
The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Jabir is weak (declared weak by al-Bayhaqi) and the hadith of Abd al-Rahman occurred before Jumu'ah was prescribed and without the Prophet's permission, so it is not valid evidence.
Thus the Shafi'i proofs are not accepted in Hanafi usul.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Hanifa holds that the minimum congregation is three besides the imam, while Abu Yusuf says two suffice. The text states that Abu Yusuf's view is 'asahh' (more correct) because the dual also conveys the meaning of gathering (جمعة).
Imam Muhammad's view is not mentioned here but generally aligns with Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and tarjih
The text explicitly gives tarjih to Abu Yusuf's view by saying 'وقوله أصح' (his statement is more correct). Therefore, the relied-upon position for fatwa is that two men besides the imam suffice for Jumu'ah.
This is an example of an intra-Hanafi tarjih within the same school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجماعة وهم ثلاثة أي سوى الإمام، ولو كانوا غير الثلاثة الذين حضروا الخطبة، وإنما قلنا سوى الإمام؛ لأن الجماعة شرط على حدة وكذا الإمام فلا يعتبر أحدهما؛ ولأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا نُودِيَ لِلصَّلاةِ مِنْ يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذكر الله له (الجمعة:٩) يقتضي مناديا وذاكرا والساعين؛ لأن قوله: "اسعوا" جمع، وأقله اثنان المنادي ثلاثة ومع وقال الشافعي: أربعون رجلاً أحرارا مقيمين سوى الإمام لا يطعنون صيفاً ولا شتاء إلا ظعن حاجة؛ لما عن جابر الله أنه قال: مضت السنة أن في كل ثلاثة أماماً، وفي أربعين فما فوقها جمعة وأضحى وفطراً، والحديث عبد الرحمن عن بن مالك قال: أول من جمع بنا سعد بن زرارة، قلت: كم كنتم؟ قال: أربعين، ولنا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَتَرَكُوكَ قَائِماً (الجمعة: ١١) أي قائما تخطب؛ لأنه لم يبق معه عليه إلا اثنا عشر رجلاً أنها عقدت باثني عشر رجلاً، وحديث جابر الله و ضعفه أهل النقل، حتى قال البيهقي: لا يحتج بمثله، وكذا حديث عبد الرحمن؛ لأنه كان قبل مقدم النبي الله المدينة قبل أن تفرض الجمعة وكان بغير إذنه، وعن أبي يوسف أدنى الجماعة اثنان سوى الإمام، وقوله أصح؛ لأن في المثنى معنى الاجتماع، والجمعة منبئة عن الاجتماع. (فتح)
And the congregation is three, i.e., besides the imam. And they need not be the same three who attended the khutbah. We said 'besides the imam' because the congregation is a separate condition, and likewise the imam, so one is not considered the other. And because Allah's statement: 'And when the call is proclaimed for the prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (62:9) implies a caller, a rememberer, and those hastening; since 'hasten' is plural, its minimum is two, so the caller makes three. Al-Shafi'i said: Forty free resident men besides the imam, who do not travel in summer or winter except for need; based on the hadith of Jabir that he said: 'The sunnah has passed that every three have an imam, and for forty and above there is Jumu'ah, Eid al-Adha, and Eid al-Fitr.' And the hadith of Abd al-Rahman from Ibn Malik: 'The first to gather us was Sa'd ibn Zurarah; I said: How many were you? He said: Forty.' And our proof is the statement of Allah: 'And they left you standing' (62:11) i.e., standing preaching, because none remained with him except twelve men that it was concluded with twelve men. The hadith of Jabir was declared weak by hadith scholars, even al-Bayhaqi said: Such is not used as evidence. Similarly the hadith of Abd al-Rahman because it was before the Prophet's arrival in Medina before Jumu'ah was prescribed and without his permission. And from Abu Yusuf: the minimum congregation is two besides the imam, and his statement is more correct because in the dual there is the meaning of gathering, and Jumu'ah denotes gathering. (Fath)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition of congregation for Jumu'ah. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that at least three men besides the imam are required. This is derived from the verse 'hasten to the remembrance of Allah' which implies a caller (the mu'adhdhin), a rememberer (the imam), and those hastening (the congregation). The plural 'hasten' requires at least two, so total three plus the imam equals four? Actually careful: they say 'three besides the imam' meaning the congregation itself is three (so total including imam is four). The text says 'three besides the imam'. The proof: 'اسعوا' is plural, minimum two, so caller (imam?) plus two = three? The text says: 'أقله اثنان المنادي ثلاثة' meaning the minimum of those hastening is two; the caller (mu'adhdhin) or the imam makes three. They specify 'three besides the imam' as the condition. Imam al-Shafi'i requires forty resident free men. The Hanafi response is that the Shafi'i proofs (hadith of Jabir and Ibn Malik) are weak or occurred before the prescription of Jumu'ah. There is also an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf says two besides the imam suffice, and the text says his view is 'asahh' (more correct). So the mufta bihi may be the view of Abu Yusuf? The text states 'وقوله أصح' (his statement is more correct). So it is a tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): The minimum number of participants besides the imam for Jumu'ah to be valid.
الإمام (al-imam): The leader of the prayer; not counted in the congregation number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Three men besides the imam.
B) Two men besides the imam.
C) Forty free resident men.
D) One man besides the imam.

Key Takeaway
For Jumu'ah, the Hanafi school holds that a congregation of two or three besides the imam is sufficient, with Abu Yusuf's view of two being the most correct (asahh) for fatwa.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Congregation Dispersing Before Sujud in Jumu'ah
Ruling when congregation flees before sujud of Jumu'ah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding Jumu'ah when the congregation disperses before sujud, and apply the ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
If congregation flees before ruku' and sujud, Jumu'ah is invalid per Abu Hanifa; after sujud, all agree it's valid.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi difference regarding a critical condition of Jumu'ah: the presence of a congregation. The passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies when dispersal invalidates the prayer. Understanding this dispute sharpens your appreciation of how conditions (shurut) interact with the commencement of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
Jumu'ah requires a congregation of men. The condition is the presence of a sufficient number (usually three besides the imam) for the prayer to be valid. The passage discusses when the loss of this condition affects validity.
Note: The precise number is not discussed here.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that if the congregation flees before the imam performs ruku' and sujud, Jumu'ah becomes invalid. The condition must persist through the essential parts of the prayer.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that once the prayer has commenced (i.e., after the takbir), later dispersal does not invalidate Jumu'ah. They consider the condition fulfilled by the initial presence.
4
Note the point of agreement
If dispersal occurs after sujud, all agree Jumu'ah remains valid. After sujud, the prayer is considered firmly established.
5
Apply to a scenario
If only women and children remain (i.e., no valid congregation), according to Abu Hanifa, Jumu'ah is invalid and must be prayed as Zuhr. The Sahibayn would likely allow completion if the prayer had started.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن نفروا قبل سجوده بطلت [الجمعة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا تبطل، ولو نفروا بعد السجود لا تبطل اتفاقاً. (ع)] أي إذا شرطت الجماعة فإن نفر الناس قبل أن يركع الإمام ويسجد استقبل الظهر عند أبي حنيفة وبطلت الجمعة وكذا لو بقي النساء أو الصبيان، وقالا إذا نفروا عنه بعد ما شرع في الصلاة أتم جمعة، فإن نفروا عنه بعد ما ركع = وصح من؟ أبيه كعب روي
Then if they flee before his sujud, it becomes invalid [Jumu'ah according to Abu Hanifa, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: it does not become invalid. If they flee after sujud, it does not become invalid by agreement. (A)] i.e., when the congregation is a condition, if the people flee before the imam has bowed and prostrated, they must start Zuhr according to Abu Hanifa, and Jumu'ah becomes invalid. Similarly, if only women or children remain. They (Sahibayn) said: If they flee from him after he has begun the prayer, he completes Jumu'ah. If they flee after he has bowed... and ? from his father Ka'b narrated.

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of Jumu'ah if the congregation disperses before completing the prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, if the congregation (the required number of men) flees before the imam performs ruku' and sujud, the Jumu'ah becomes invalid, and they must pray Zuhr instead. This is because the congregation is considered a condition for Jumu'ah, and if it is lost early, the prayer is nullified. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), if the congregation flees after the prayer has commenced, the imam continues and completes Jumu'ah. If they flee after sujud, all agree Jumu'ah is valid. The text also notes that if only women or children remain (i.e., no sufficient congregation), Jumu'ah is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. The OCR is unclear at the end, but the core ruling is captured.

Key Terms
النفر (al-nafr): To flee or disperse; removal of the congregation from the prayer.
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration; after sujud, the prayer is considered firmly established.

Key Takeaway
The validity of Jumu'ah after congregation dispersal depends on when it occurs: before ruku' and sujud (dispute) or after (agreement).

Conditions of the Friday Khutbah: Minimal Dhikr and Hanafi Position
Explains minimal required dhikr and conditions of the Friday sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimal required content of the Friday khutbah and explain why standing and purity are recommended but not obligatory in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A single phrase of dhikr with intention suffices for the Friday khutbah; standing and purity are sunnah, not fard.

The Friday khutbah is a central element of Jumu'ah, but what does the Hanafi school require for its validity? This lesson examines the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, which states that a single tahmeed, tahleel, or tasbeeh is sufficient. We will explore the proofs from Quran and practice, and understand why the Hanafi school distinguishes the khutbah from prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its minimal ruling
The Friday khutbah is the act under discussion. The source states that a single phrase of dhikr (tahmeed, tahleel, or tasbeeh) suffices for its content. This is the minimal requirement for validity.
The khutbah itself is a condition for Jumu'ah prayer; its validity depends on fulfilling this content.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof for this minimal content is the Quranic verse: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (62:9). The word 'dhikr' is general, encompassing any remembrance. Additionally, the practice of Caliph Uthman (ra) when he became tongue-tied showed that even a simple 'Alhamdulillah' sufficed.
The dalil is from Quran and sunna (action of a companion).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase is 'dhikr' in the verse. In Hanafi usul, a general command ('amm) indicates obligation (wujub) for all instances. Since 'dhikr' is general, any form of divine remembrance can fulfill it.
The Shafi'i school also uses this verse but interprets it differently regarding standing and purity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i requires standing and ritual purity (taharah) for the khutbah, analogizing it to two rak'ahs of prayer. The Hanafi response is that the khutbah contradicts the form of prayer (turning away from qibla, speaking), so it cannot stand in place of prayer.
This is a key difference in usul: analogy (qiyas) vs. istihsan (juristic preference) or textual interpretation.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because the khutbah's form (speaking, turning) is incompatible with prayer. Therefore, conditions of prayer like standing and purity are only recommended (sunnah), not obligatory. The minimal dhikr with intention is sufficient for validity.
The mufta bihi position: a single tahmeed/tahleel/tasbeeh with niyyah suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة
بجلسة بينهما بطهارة قائما وكفت تحميدة أو تهليلة أو تسبيحة،
بطهارة متعلق لمحذوف أي يخطب بطهارة حال كونه قائماً. (ط) قائماً : وعند الشافعي: لا تجوز إلا قائماً، ولا بدون الطهارة؛ لأنها قائم مقام ركعتين وعندنا لا تقوم مقامهما؛ لأنها تنافي الصلاة؛ لما فيها من استدبار القبلة والكلام، فلا يشترط لها ما يشترط للصلاة. (فتح) تحميدة: إنما اكتفى بالتحميدة ونحوها؛ لإطلاق قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسَعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ الله (الجمعة: 9) وعن عثمان الله أنه قال: الحمد لله، فارتج عليه فقال: إنكم إلى إمام فعال أحوج منكم إلى إمام قوال، وإن أبا بكر وعمر ما كانا يعدان لهذا المقام مقالاً، وستأتيكم الخطب من بعد، وأستغفر الله لي ولكم وقالا: لا يجوز إلا إذا كان يسمى خطبة عادة، وقيل: أقله قدر التشهد. (فتح مسكين تسبيحة أي قوله: سبحان الله بشرط نية الخطبة في الكل، حتى لو حمد العطاسه لم تنب عنها. (ط، ع)
Chapter of Friday Prayer: With a sitting between them, in a state of purity, standing, and a single praising, declaration of oneness, or glorification suffices. Purity is attached to an omitted [word], meaning he delivers the khutbah in purity as a state of standing. (T) Standing: According to al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible except standing, and not without purity, because it stands in place of two rak'ahs. According to us, it does not stand in place of two rak'ahs, because it contradicts prayer, due to turning away from the qibla and speaking, so what is required for prayer is not required for it. (Fath) A praising: He sufficed with a praising and the like due to the general meaning of His statement: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (al-Jumu'ah:9). And from Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'Praise be to Allah,' but his speech was closed. So he said: 'You are in more need of an imam who acts than an imam who speaks. Abu Bakr and Umar did not count talking as part of this station. Khutbahs will come to you after this. I seek forgiveness for you and for me.' And they said: It is not permissible unless it is customarily called a khutbah, and it was said: its minimum is the amount of tashahhud. (Fath Miskin) 'Tasbeeh' means his saying: Subhan Allah, with the condition of intention of the khutbah in all of it, so that if he praises a sneeze, it does not count for it. (T, A)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Friday prayer by establishing the essential conditions of the khutbah. The matn states that the khutbah is performed with a sitting between its two parts, in a state of ritual purity (taharah), while standing, and that a single phrase of praise (tahmeed), declaration of tawhid (tahleel), or glorification (tasbeeh) is sufficient for its content. The sharh then explains these conditions in detail. First, 'purity' and 'standing' are discussed: the Hanafi position does not require them as strictly as prayer, because the khutbah is not analogous to prayer—it involves turning away from the qibla and speaking. The Shafi'i view requires both, but the Hanafi response is that the khutbah is a separate act. Next, the minimal dhikr is justified by the Quranic command to hasten to the remembrance of Allah, and by the practice of Uthman (ra) when he became tongue-tied during his first khutbah—he simply said 'Alhamdulillah' and then improvised. Some scholars require the khutbah to be of a customary length or at least the amount of tashahhud. Finally, the condition of niyyah (intention) is stressed: the dhikr must be intended as part of the khutbah; a random praise of a sneeze does not count.

Key Terms
تحميدة (tahmeedah): A single phrase of praising Allah, e.g., 'Alhamdulillah'
تهليلة (tahleelah): A single declaration of tawhid, 'La ilaha illa Allah'
تسبيحة (tasbeehah): A single glorification, 'Subhan Allah'
نية (niyyah): Intention that the dhikr is offered as part of the khutbah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Surah al-Fatihah
B) A single tahmeed, tahleel, or tasbeeh
C) At least three verses of the Quran
D) The tashahhud

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a very brief Friday khutbah—a single phrase of dhikr with proper intention suffices, while standing and purity are only recommended.

Effect of Congregation Dispersal in Friday Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on congregation persistence in Friday prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on congregation dispersal during Friday prayer and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The congregation is only required at the start of Friday prayer; dispersal after initiation does not invalidate it according to the Sahibayn.

In this lesson, we examine a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the Friday prayer. The passage discusses whether the congregation must remain present throughout the prayer or only at its start. Understanding this disagreement reveals how the Hanafi school defines conditions (shurut) for prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the three positions: Abu Hanifa says Friday is invalid if dispersal occurs before sajdah; Sahibayn say it remains valid; Zufar says congregation must persist throughout.
Note the timing threshold: before or after the imam's prostration.
2
Understand the timing element
Focus on the key moment: before the imam's sajdah (complete rak'ah) versus after. Abu Hanifa's ruling hinges on the prayer being fully established only when a complete rak'ah is performed.
Sajdah here signals completion of the first full rak'ah.
3
Analyze the underlying principle
The dispute revolves around the nature of the congregation condition: Abu Hanifa considers it a condition for the contract's firmness (shart in'iqaad) that must persist until the prayer is established; Sahibayn consider it only a condition for the beginning (shart shuru').
Compare with Zufar who treats it as a condition for performance (shart ada') requiring continuity.
4
Evaluate the analogy with khutbah
Sahibayn analogize congregation to the khutbah, which is required at the start but not during the prayer. Abu Hanifa distinguishes because the prayer itself begins with the takbir and is incomplete without a full rak'ah.
This analogy is central to the Sahibayn's reasoning.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, if the congregation disperses early, the imam must decide: according to Abu Hanifa, he switches to Zuhr; according to Sahibayn, he continues Friday. Fatwa generally follows the Sahibayn for flexibility.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the imam's action during the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبل سجوده: أي الإمام بعد أن أحرموا معه. [رمز الحقائق: ٩٩/١] بطلت [الجمعة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا : لا تبطل، ولو نفروا بعد السجود لا تبطل اتفاقاً. (ع)] أي إذا شرطت الجماعة فإن نفر الناس قبل أن يركع الإمام ويسجد استقبل الظهر عند أبي حنيفة وبطلت الجمعة وكذا لو بقي النساء أو الصبيان، وقالا إذا نفروا عنه بعد ما شرع في الصلاة أتم جمعة، فإن نفروا عنه بعد ما ركع = وسجد بني عليه الجمعة في قولهم جميعاً خلافاً لزفر، والأصل فيه: أن الجماعة شرط تأكد الانعقاد بالسجدة عنده، وعندهما شرط الشروع، وعند زفر: للأداء وهو يقول: إن الجماعة لما كانت شرطا فلابد من دوامها كالوقت، وهما يقولان إن الجماعة شرط الانعقاد والانعقاد بالشروع فلا يشترط دوامها كالخطبة، بل هي الشروع مستغن عنها، ولأبي حنيفة: أن شروع الصلاة إنما يتم بتمام الركعة؛ لأن ما دونها ليست بصلاة فلابد من دوامها إلى السجود بخلاف الخطبة؛ لأنها تنافي الصلاة فلا يشترط دوامها. (مستخلص، عيني)
Before his prostration: i.e., the imam after they [the congregation] entered ihram with him. [Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 99/1] It becomes invalid: Friday [for Abu Hanifa, and the two said: it does not become invalid]. Even if they disperse after prostration, it does not become invalid by agreement. (A) That is, if the congregation is a condition, and the people disperse before the imam bows and prostrates, he prays Zuhr according to Abu Hanifa, and Friday is invalid. Similarly if only women or boys remain. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: if they dispersed after he started the prayer, he completes Friday. If they dispersed after he bowed and prostrated, the Friday is built upon it according to all of them, contrary to Zufar. The principle: The congregation is a condition for the firmness of the contract [binding] by the prostration according to him [Abu Hanifa]; according to the two, it is a condition for beginning; according to Zufar, it is for performance. He says: Since the congregation is a condition, its continuity is required like the time. The two say: The congregation is a condition for contract, and the contract is by beginning, so its continuity is not required, like the khutbah. Rather, once begun, it is independent of it. For Abu Hanifa: Beginning the prayer is only completed by completion of a rak'ah, because less than that is not prayer, so continuity until prostration is required, unlike the khutbah because it contradicts prayer, so its continuity is not required. (Mustakhlas, Ayni)
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage addresses what happens if the congregation for Friday prayer disperses during the prayer. The ruling differentiates based on timing: before the imam's sajdah (prostration), Abu Hanifa holds that the Friday prayer is invalid, and the participants must pray Zuhr instead; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that Friday remains valid. After the imam's sajdah, all agree that Friday is valid even if dispersal occurs. Zufar holds that congregation must persist throughout the prayer like the time condition, but the majority disagrees. The underlying principle: Abu Hanifa sees the congregation as a condition for the completion of a full rak'ah; the Sahibayn see it as a condition only for initiating the prayer, analogous to the khutbah which is not required to continue during the prayer. The text then clarifies that if dispersal happens after bowing and prostrating (i.e., after a complete rak'ah), all except Zufar agree the prayer is valid.

Key Terms
شرط انعقاد (shart in'iqaad): A condition for the validity (contract) of the prayer—required at the start
شرط أداء (shart ada'): A condition for performance—must persist throughout the act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the Friday congregation disperses before the imam prostrates according to the Sahibayn?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and they must pray Zuhr
B) The prayer is still valid as Friday
C) They must repeat the prayer
D) The imam alone completes two rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the congregation's presence is only a condition for initiating Friday prayer, not for its continuation, so dispersal after the start does not invalidate it.

Public Permission for Friday Prayer
Explains that public permission from the sultan is a condition for holding Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of public permission for the validity of Friday prayer and apply it to distinguish valid and invalid scenarios.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is invalid without the ruler's public permission — a private congregation cannot substitute.

In the Hanafi school, Friday prayer (Jumu'ah) is a special communal act that requires public authorization. This lesson examines the condition that the ruler must permit general access to the prayer. We will see how the text condemns locking doors or holding private Friday prayers, even by the ruler himself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Friday prayer (salat al-Jumu'ah) is the act under discussion. The text states a condition for its validity: public permission from the ruler.
The condition is about validity, not obligation.
2
Understand the condition (shart)
The condition is al-idhn al-'amm (general permission) from the sultan/imam. This means opening the doors of the mosque and allowing all Muslims to attend.
Permission must be explicit and public.
3
Analyze the counterexamples
Two invalid scenarios: (1) A group locks the mosque doors and prays Friday; (2) The ruler prays with his army privately in his house or mosque. Both lack public permission.
Even the ruler must grant public access.
4
Examine the border case
If the ruler opens his palace and permits entry, the prayer is valid but makruh because he bypasses the congregational mosque's right.
Makruh tanzihi? The text does not specify level.
5
Conclude the legal effect
Without public permission, Friday prayer is invalid (la yajuz). With permission but not in a proper mosque, it is valid but disliked.
The condition ensures the public character of Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والإذن العام بالرفع عطف على المرفوعات قبله وشرط أدائها أيضاً الإذن العام من السلطان بأن تفتح أبواب الجوامع للواردين] أي الإذن العام من الإمام بفتح أبواب الجامع والإذن للناس حتى لو اجتمعت جماعة في الجامع وأغلقوا الباب وجمعوا لم يجز ذلك، وكذا السلطان إذا أراد أن يصلي الجمعة بعسكره في داره أو الجامع لم يجز؛ لعدم الإذن، وإن فتح باب قصره وأذن للناس بالدخول فيه يجوز ويكره؛ لأنه لم يقض حق المسجد الجامع. [رمز الحقائق: ٩٩/١] (عيني، مسكين)
And the general permission: with raf' [case ending] as a conjunction to the nominatives before it. A condition for its performance also is the general permission from the sultan, by opening the doors of the congregational mosques to those entering. That is, the general permission from the imam [ruler] to open the doors of the mosque and permission for the people. So if a group gathers in the mosque and locks the door and holds Friday, that is not permissible. Similarly, if the sultan wants to pray Friday with his army in his house or in the mosque, it is not permissible due to lack of permission. And if he opens the door of his palace and permits people to enter, it is permissible but disliked (makruh) because he has not fulfilled the right of the congregational mosque. [Rumuz al-Haqa'iq 99/1] (Ayni, Miskin)
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage states that the Friday prayer requires public permission (idhn 'amm) from the Muslim ruler (sultan/imam). This condition means the ruler must permit the general public to attend Friday prayer in mosques designated for this purpose. If a group locks themselves in a mosque and holds Friday without public access, it is invalid. Even the ruler himself cannot pray Friday with his soldiers privately in his palace or a mosque without opening the doors to the public. If he opens his palace and permits people to enter, the prayer is valid but makruh because he is not using a proper congregational mosque. This condition ensures the public nature of the weekly gathering.

Key Terms
الإذن العام (al-idhn al-'amm): The general permission from the Muslim ruler allowing public access to Friday prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid because they have a congregation
B) The prayer is invalid because there is no public permission
C) The prayer is valid but makruh
D) They must first notify the ruler

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is only valid when the ruler grants public permission; any attempt to hold it privately invalidates the prayer.

Conditions for Obligation of Friday Prayer
Condition listing for Friday prayer obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven conditions for the obligation of Friday prayer and identify which exemptions apply to whom.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is fard 'ayn only on the free, healthy, resident, sighted, walking male.

Friday prayer is a weekly obligation that carries great reward, but not every Muslim is required to attend. The Hanafi school identifies specific conditions that must be met for it to become binding. In this lesson, we examine the text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq that catalogues these conditions, unpacking each one and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
List the primary conditions from the text
The first sentence lists the conditions: iqamah (residence), dhukurah (masculinity), sihha (health), hurriyya (freedom), salamat al-'aynayn (soundness of eyes) and salamat al-rijlayn (soundness of legs = ability to walk).
Note that the author mentions 'soundness of eyes and legs' separately from 'health'.
2
Identify the exemptions from the commentary
The text explains that the sick, blind, and those who cannot walk are exempt. Additionally, the Fath commentary adds imprisonment, fear, and heavy rain as excuses that lift the obligation.
Blindness exemption holds even if a guide is available.
3
Understand the rationale for the blindness exemption
The text argues that a blind person is not considered capable even if they can hire a guide, because capability through another is not true capability (al-qadir bi-qudrat al-ghayr la yu'adu qadiran).
This is a key Hanafi principle: personal capacity is required.
4
Recognize the terminology nuance
The author wishes the phrasing were 'existence of sight and ability to walk' to include the one-eyed and the lame who can manage. He also notes that 'soundness of eyes' is a specific example under 'health' (عطف الخاص على العام), because in custom, blindness is not called 'illness' but it is a medical condition.
This linguistic precision avoids ambiguity in legal rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط وجوبها الإقامة والذكورة والصحة والحرية وسلامة العينين والرجلين، أي وجوب الجمعة فلا تجب على المريض بعد ووسلامة العينين والرجلين فلا تجب على الأعمى وإن كان له ما يستأجر به القائد عند الإمام؛ لأن القادر بقدرة الغير لا يعد قادراً، وكذا لا تجب عليه إذا كان له مملوك يقوده، فلو أبدل المصنف قوله: "وسلامة العينين والرجلين" بقوله: "ووجود البصر والقدرة على المشي لكان أولى؛ ليفيد وجوبها على الأعور والأعرج بالغير المانع من قدرة المشي بلا مشقة وعطف سلامة العينين على الصحة من عطف الخاص على العام؛ لأن عدم سلامة العينين والرجلين من الأمراض عند الأطباء إلا أنهما في العرف لا يعدان مرضاً فلهذا خصهما بالذكر؛ ولأن فيها خلافاً، وبقي من الأعذار الحبس والخوف والمطر الشديد فيشترط بوجوبها عدم هذه الأشياء. (فتح) والرجلين: أي وسلامة الرجلين يعني قدرة المشي فلا تجب على المقعد ومقطوعهما. (ع)
And the condition of its obligation: residence, masculinity, health, freedom, and soundness of the eyes and legs. That is, the obligation of Friday, so it is not obligatory on the sick. And soundness of eyes and legs: so it is not obligatory on the blind, even if he has the means to hire a guide according to the Imam [Abu Hanifa?], because one who is capable by another's capability is not considered capable. Similarly, it is not obligatory on him if he has a slave to lead him. If the author had replaced his statement 'and soundness of eyes and legs' with 'and existence of sight and ability to walk' it would have been better, to indicate its obligation on the one-eyed and the lame if there is no impediment to ability to walk without hardship. And the conjunction of 'soundness of eyes' with 'health' is a conjunction of specific to general, because the lack of soundness of eyes and legs are considered illnesses by physicians, but in custom they are not considered illness, therefore he specified them. Also because there is a difference of opinion. And remaining excuses: imprisonment, fear, and heavy rain, so their absence is a condition for obligation. (Fath) And the legs: meaning soundness of the legs i.e., ability to walk, so it is not obligatory on the paralyzed or those whose legs are cut off. (A)
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage enumerates the conditions that make Friday prayer obligatory (fard) on an individual: being a resident (not a traveler), male (not female or hermaphrodite), healthy (not sick), free (not a slave), with sound eyesight and ability to walk. The text explains that blindness exempts a person even if they can afford a guide, because reliance on another's ability does not make one capable. Similarly, being unable to walk (paralyzed, leg amputated, etc.) exempts one. The author notes that the condition 'soundness of eyes and legs' is a specific subset of 'health', but they are emphasized because they are not typically seen as illnesses in common custom. Also, other excuses like imprisonment, fear of harm, and heavy rain also lift the obligation.

Key Terms
الإقامة (al-iqamah): Permanent residence in a town/city where Friday is established
الذكورة (al-dhukurah): Being male; women and hermaphrodites are exempt
صحة البصر (sihhat al-basar): Soundness of eyesight; blindness exempts even with a guide

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of Friday prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Being a resident
B) Being male
C) Being able to walk
D) Being able to read Quran

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is only obligatory on a free, healthy, resident, sighted, walking male; those who are blind, sick, paralyzed, or excused by imprisonment, fear, or heavy rain are exempt.

The Condition of Congregation in Jumu'ah: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on congregation as a condition for Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on the timing of the congregation condition in Jumu'ah and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
In Jumu'ah, does the congregation condition fire only at the start or must it linger until the sajdah? Three Hanafi imams differ.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: is congregation (jama'ah) a condition that must be present only at the commencement of Jumu'ah, throughout the prayer, or until a specific point? The answer determines the ruling for a latecomer who joins after the first sajdah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
Recognize that all Hanafi imams agree congregation is a condition for Jumu'ah, but they disagree on the timing: at the start (shart al-shuru'), throughout (shart al-ada'), or until the first sajdah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and Proof
Abu Hanifa holds that congregation is a condition for the validity (in'iqad) of the prayer, and validity is only achieved by completing a full rak'ah. Therefore, one must be with the congregation until the sajdah of the first rak'ah.
He distinguishes prayer from khutbah: khutbah is not part of prayer, so its condition does not require continuity.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Proof
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that congregation is a condition at the start (shart al-shuru'), like the khutbah. Once the prayer has begun with the congregation, the condition is fulfilled even if the congregation disbands later.
They analogize to the khutbah, which occurs before prayer but is not required to continue.
4
State Zufar's Position and Proof
Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl holds that congregation is a condition for the entire performance (shart al-ada'), so it must be present from the opening takbir to the final salam, like the condition of time.
He argues that any condition for an act requires continuity throughout that act.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Mufta Bihi
The practical difference: If a person joins after the sajdah of the first rak'ah, Abu Hanifa says he missed the congregation condition and must pray Zuhr; the Sahibayn say his Jumu'ah is valid because he started with the congregation. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view, but later scholars sometimes follow the Sahibayn for ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسجد بني عليه الجمعة في قولهم جميعاً خلافاً لزفر، والأصل فيه: أن الجماعة شرط تأكد الانعقاد بالسجدة عنده، وعندهما شرط الشروع، وعند زفر: للأداء وهو يقول: إن الجماعة لما كانت شرطا فلابد من دوامها كالوقت، وهما يقولان إن الجماعة شرط الانعقاد والانعقاد بالشروع فلا يشترط دوامها كالخطبة، بل هي الشروع مستغن عنها، ولأبي حنيفة: أن شروع الصلاة إنما يتم بتمام الركعة؛ لأن ما دونها ليست بصلاة فلابد من دوامها إلى السجود بخلاف الخطبة؛ لأنها تنافي الصلاة فلا يشترط دوامها. (مستخلص، عيني)
And he prostrated, built upon it Jumu'ah in all their sayings, contrary to Zufar. The principle in it is: the congregation is a condition for the confirmation of validity through the prostration according to him (Abu Hanifa), and according to them (Sahibayn) it is a condition for the commencement, and according to Zufar it is for performance, and he says: since the congregation is a condition, its continuity is necessary like the time, and they (Sahibayn) say: the congregation is a condition for validity and validity is at the commencement, so its continuity is not required like the khutba, rather what is at the commencement dispenses with it. And according to Abu Hanifa: the commencement of prayer is only completed by completing a rak'ah, because what is less than a rak'ah is not prayer, so its continuity is necessary until the prostration, contrary to the khutba because it is incompatible with prayer, so its continuity is not required. (Mukhtasar, Ayni)
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of congregation (jama'ah) in Friday prayer: is it a condition at the start (shart al-shuru') or throughout the prayer (shart al-ada')? The dispute arises when a person enters the Friday prayer late but catches the congregation only at the sajdah or later. According to Abu Hanifa, the congregation is a condition for the validity of the prayer, but he holds that the prayer's commencement (shuru') is only complete with a full rak'ah. Thus, if one joins the congregation before the end of the first rak'ah, he has fulfilled the condition; if he joins after, the congregation is missing for him. However, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that congregation is a condition only at the start (shart al-shuru'), so as long as one begins the prayer with the congregation, the condition is met even if the congregation breaks up later. Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl holds that congregation is a condition for the entire prayer (shart al-ada'), so it must be present from beginning to end. The argument uses qiyas with the khutba: the Sahibayn argue that just as the khutba is not required to continue after the start, similarly congregation. Abu Hanifa responds that prayer is different from khutba because a partial rak'ah is not considered prayer, and the congregation must continue until the sajdah to satisfy the condition.

Key Terms
شرط الانعقاد (sharṭ al-in‘iqād): A condition for the validity of the prayer at its start.
شرط الشروع (sharṭ al-shurū‘): A condition required at the beginning of the act.
شرط الأداء (sharṭ al-adā’): A condition required throughout the entire act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is congregation required to continue until the sajdah?
A) Because the congregation must be present for the entire prayer like time
B) Because the start of prayer is only complete with a full rak'ah, and a partial rak'ah is not prayer
C) Because prostration is the most important part of the prayer
D) Because the Prophet always prostrated with the congregation

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the congregation condition for Jumu'ah, according to the mufta bihi, requires being with the congregation until the sajdah of the first rak'ah; a latecomer after that must pray Zuhr.

Non-Obligated Persons Leading Friday Prayer
Ruling with proof on non-obligated persons leading Friday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on non-obligated persons leading and forming a Friday congregation, explain the qiyas proof, and compare it with Zufar's position.

Core Idea
Non-obligated persons can lead Friday – the concession is in attendance, not capability.

Friday prayer is not obligatory on certain individuals such as travelers, slaves, and the sick. But does that mean they cannot lead or form a congregation? The Hanafi school says they can, based on a clear analogy. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and the disagreement within and outside the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an adult male traveler, slave, or sick person leading Friday prayer or being part of the congregation. The ruling is that it is valid (jā'iz) and suffices for the obligatory Zuhr.
The ruling applies even if the imam and all followers are from these categories.
2
Locate the dalil
The Hanafi proof is qiyas with a traveler who fasts in Ramadan: fasting is not obligatory on a traveler, but if he fasts, it counts. Similarly, if a non-obligated person performs Friday, it counts.
The illa (cause) is that the obligation was lifted as a concession, not due to a defect in the person.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and the Shafi'i school hold that such a person cannot lead because Friday is not obligatory on them, analogizing to a child or woman.
The disagreement affects whether a traveler imam is acceptable.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes: a child is not eligible for imāma at all, and a woman cannot lead men. The traveler, slave, etc. are eligible; the concession only removes the obligation to attend, not their capability.
The response uses the same qiyas but refines the illa to focus on eligibility.
5
Determine the thamarah
Practical consequence: A traveler imam can lead Friday for travelers and residents. According to Zufar, the prayer would be invalid. Shafi'is require 40 free, resident men for validity.
Hanafis also hold that the congregation is valid even if all followers are non-obligated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لا جمعة عليه إن أدّاها جاز عن فرض الوقت، وللمسافر والعبد والمريض أن يؤم دك ف فيها، وتنعقد بهم
أي حضر الجمعة أدائه الجمعة أي الجماعة للجمعة هو الصحيح المقيم الحر وكره للمعذور والمسجون. أي تحريماً مثل المريض والمسافر في الحبس صلاته صلاة الجمعة تحريماً وعند الثلاثة لا يجوز لا جمعة عليه مثل المسافر والمرأة والعبد والمريض والشيخ الفاني ونحوهم. (ع) جاز عن فرض الوقت: [وهو الظهر؛ لأن امتناع الوجوب كان للتخفيف فإذا تحمله جاز كالمسافر إذا صام. (ط، ع)] أي الذين لا جمعة عليهم إذا حضروا الجمعة فذلك على ثلاثة أقسام: الأول: أنه ليس بأهل للوجوب كالصبي والمجنون فصلاة الصبي نافلة ولا صلاة للمجنون أصلا والثاني: أنهم من أهل الوجوب كالمريض والمسافر وغيرهما يجزيهم، وسقط عنهم فرض الوقت؛ لأن امتناع الوجوب عليهم لم يكن لمعنى في الصلاة، بل للحرج والضرر ، فإذا تحملوا التحقوا في الأداء بغيرهم، الثالث: أنه يوجد في حقهم شرائط الوجوب لكن لا شرائط الأداء كالمصر ،وغيره بأن كانت جماعة من الشافعين يصلون الجمعة في موضع اجتمع فيه أربعون من الأحرار، فإن اقتدى بهم حنفي لا يجزيه عن الظهر؛ لأن ما صلى ليس بجمعة في زعمه فلا يسقط عنه الفرض الأصلي. (مستخلص، فتح) أن يؤم فيها: الحصر المستفاد من تقديم الخبر الظرفي بالنسبة لمن لا تصح إمامته كالصبي والمرأة لا مطلقاً، وقال زفر : لا يجوز لهم الإمامة في الجمعة؛ لأنها غير واجبة عليهم كالصبي والمرأة ولنا أنهم أهل للإمامة، وإنما سقط الوجوب للرخصة، فإذا حضروا تقع فرضا كالمسافر إذا صام، بخلاف الصبي؛ لأنه غير أهل، وبخلاف المرأة؛ لأنها لا تصلح إماماً للرجال. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥٣٣/١] (فتح) وتنعقد بهم: [حتى لو كان خلفه مسافر وعبد ومريض فقط جازت الجمعة خلافاً للشافعي. (ط،ع)] أي بالمذكورين من المسافر والعبد والمريض؛ لأنهم إذا صلحوا للإمامة فلأن يصلحوا للاقتداء بالطريق الأولى. (فتح)
And whoever has no Friday [obligation] upon him, if he performs it, it suffices for the obligatory time. And for the traveler, slave, and sick, they may lead in it, and it is valid with them. Meaning: if he attends Friday, its performance is Friday, i.e., the congregation for Friday is the sound, resident, free man, and it is disliked for the excused and imprisoned, i.e., prohibition, like the sick and traveler in prison. His prayer of Friday is prohibited, and according to the three (Zufar and Shafi'i?) it is not valid. Whoever has no Friday upon him like the traveler, woman, slave, sick, decrepit old man, and their like. (A) It suffices for the obligatory time: [i.e., it is Zuhr, because the omission of obligation was for alleviation, so if he undertakes it, it is valid, like a traveler who fasts.] (T, A) That is, those who have no Friday upon them, if they attend Friday, that is of three types: first: they are not eligible for obligation, like the child and the insane, so the child's prayer is voluntary and the insane has no prayer at all; second: they are eligible for obligation, like the sick and traveler and others, it suffices for them and the obligation of the time is dropped, because the omission of obligation on them was not due to a meaning in the prayer, but due to hardship and harm, so if they undertake it, they join in performance with others; third: that the conditions of obligation exist for them but not the conditions of performance, like the Egyptian? etc., such that a group of Shafi'is pray Friday in a place where forty free men gather, and a Hanafi follows them, it does not suffice for Zuhr because what he prayed is not Friday in his belief, so the original obligation does not fall from him. (Mukhtasar, Fath) That he lead in it: the restriction derived from placing the adverbial phrase first in relation to those whose leadership is not valid, like the child and woman, not absolutely. And Zufar said: they are not allowed to lead in Friday because it is not obligatory on them like the child and woman. And we argue: they are eligible for leadership, and the obligation fell only due to a concession, so if they attend, it falls as an obligation like the traveler who fasts, contrary to the child because he is not eligible, and contrary to the woman because she is not fit to lead men. [Tabyin al-Haqaiq 1/533] (Fath) And it is valid with them: [even if only a traveler, slave, and sick are behind him, the Friday is valid, contrary to Shafi'i.] (T, A) Meaning by the mentioned ones: traveler, slave, and sick; because if they are qualified to lead, then they are even more qualified to follow, by a fortiori argument. (Fath)
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage covers several interrelated rulings. First, it states that persons upon whom Friday is not obligatory (such as a traveler, slave, sick person) may still perform it, and it will suffice for their Zuhr obligation. The commentary explains that this is like a traveler choosing to fast in Ramadan. Then it addresses the issue of leading prayer: these same individuals are allowed to lead the Friday prayer, contrary to Zufar who argues that since Friday is not obligatory on them, they cannot lead. The Hanafi response is that obligation fell due to a concession, not due to any defect in their eligibility; thus, when they choose to attend, it becomes obligatory for them at that moment. Finally, it discusses the validity of the congregation: if the followers are only those who are not obligated (like a traveler, slave, and sick), the Friday prayer is still valid. This contrasts with the Shafi'i school, which requires 40 fully responsible residents. The commentary also notes an exception: if a Hanafi follows a Shafi'i congregation that holds Friday with 40 free men in a place where the Hanafi does not consider it a valid Friday due to lack of permission or other conditions, then his performance does not count as Friday, and he must still pray Zuhr.

Key Terms
من لا جمعة عليه (man lā jumu‘a ‘alayh): A person for whom Friday prayer is not obligatory, such as a traveler, slave, woman, sick, or decrepit old person.
أم فيها (amma fīhā): To lead the Friday prayer as imam.
تنعقد بهم (tan‘aqid bihim): The Friday prayer is valid with them as followers (i.e., the congregation is established by their presence).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a traveler leads Friday prayer and only other travelers and a slave follow him, the prayer is:
A) Invalid, because the imam is not obligated to attend Friday
B) Valid and counts as Friday for all
C) Valid only if there is at least one resident among the followers
D) Invalid, because slaves cannot be followers in Friday

Key Takeaway
Non-obligated persons can lead Friday prayer and form a valid congregation because the concession is in the obligation to attend, not in their eligibility for leadership.

Zuhr Before Friday: Hanafi Ruling and Nullification
Ruling on praying Zuhr before Friday and its nullification if one then goes to Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying Zuhr before Friday for a person without excuse, explain the inter-madhhab dispute, and apply the rule of nullification upon proceeding to Friday.

Core Idea
Praying Zuhr before Friday is valid but sinful for the unexcused; if you then go to Friday, your Zuhr turns into nafl.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on a person without excuse who prays Zuhr before the Friday prayer. The text explains why such a prayer is makruh tahrimi (prohibited) yet valid, and how it becomes nullified if the person proceeds to the Friday prayer. It also contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Zufar and the other three schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text addresses two cases: (1) praying Zuhr before Friday for an unexcused person, and (2) then proceeding to Friday after having prayed Zuhr.
The ruling on the first scenario is that it is makruh tahrimi but valid; the second scenario results in nullification of the Zuhr.
2
Understand 'karaha' as prohibition
In this context, 'karaha' means makruh tahrimi (prohibited), not mere dislike. The commentary clarifies that the author intended 'haram' because the person abandons the stronger obligation.
The term 'kariha' is used technically in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rationale
The Hanafi school argues that Zuhr is the default fard because the individual can fulfill its conditions, whereas Friday depends on conditions beyond his control. He is commanded to drop Zuhr for Friday, so praying Zuhr is a sin but the prayer is valid.
This rationale is based on the principle that the original obligation (Zuhr) persists unless the substitute (Friday) is possible.
4
Examine the opposing view
Zufar and the three other schools consider Friday as the original obligation when conditions are met, thus Zuhr is only a substitute and invalid when the original can be performed.
This is an example of a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different usul principles.
5
Determine the consequence of proceeding
If after praying Zuhr one proceeds to Friday (e.g., leaves home heading to the mosque), the Zuhr prayer becomes invalid (batil) and turns into a nafl (voluntary) prayer, regardless of whether one catches Friday.
The commentator notes that 'fasād' (corruption) is a more precise term than 'buṭlān'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لا عذر له لو صلّى الظهر قبلها كره، فإن سعى إليها بطل،
قيد بعدم العذر؛ لأن المعذور إذا صلى الظهر قبل الإمام لا كراهة اتفاقاً، وقوله: "كره" أراد به حرم؛ لأنه ترك الفرض القطعي باتفاقهم الذي هو أكد من الظهر، وعند زفر والثلاثة لا يجوز، وهذا مبني على أن الأصل عندهم هو الجمعة، والظهر بدل عنها، فلا يصار إليه مع القدرة على الأصل ولنا: أن الفرض هو الظهر لقدرته عليه دون الجمعة لتوقفها على شرائط لا تتم به وحده إلا أنه مأمور بإسقاط الظهر بالجمعة، فيكون بتركه مسيئاً، فيكره ، وقيد بقوله: "قبلها"، لأنه لو صلى بالظهر بعدها في منزله لا يكره اتفاقاً. (فتح، عيني) سعى: الذي صلى الظهر مثلاً إلى الجمعة بعد ما صلى الظهر بأن انفصل عن باب داره والإمام فيها. (ط،ع) بطل: [ أي بطل ظهره وانقلب نفلا أدركها أو لا بلا فرق بين معذور وغيره على المذهب. (ط)] أي إن أدى الظهر ثم سعى إلى الجمعة بطل الظهر المؤدى وانقلب نفلاً، والتعبير بالفساد أولى؛ لأن البطلان هو الذي يفوت
And whoever has no excuse, if he prays Zuhr before it (Friday), it is disliked (makruh). Then if he proceeds to it, his Zuhr is invalidated. Qualified by the absence of excuse, because the excused person if he prays Zuhr before the imam, there is no dislike by agreement. And his saying: "disliked" he intended prohibition (haram), because he leaves the definite obligatory by their agreement which is stronger than Zuhr. And according to Zufar and the three (other schools), it is not valid. This is based on the principle that for them the original is Friday, and Zuhr is a substitute for it, so one does not go to the substitute when able to do the original. And for us: the obligatory is Zuhr because he is able to perform it, not Friday because it depends on conditions that are not fulfilled by him alone, but he is commanded to drop Zuhr by Friday, so by abandoning it he is sinful, thus it is disliked. And he qualified by his saying "before it", because if he prays Zuhr after it in his house, there is no dislike by agreement. (Fath, Ayni) Sought: meaning one who prayed Zuhr, for example, then goes to Friday after having prayed Zuhr by leaving his door while the imam is in it. (T, A) Invalidated: [meaning his Zuhr becomes invalid and turns into optional prayer whether he catches Friday or not, no difference between excused and other according to the madhhab.] (T) That is, if he prayed Zuhr then proceeded to Friday, his performed Zuhr becomes invalid and turns into optional prayer, and the expression 'fasād' (corruption) is better because 'buṭlān' is what passes.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage discusses two related rulings. First, it is makruh (prohibited) for a person without an excuse to pray Zuhr before the Friday prayer. The commentary explains that this 'karaha' here means tahrimi (prohibition) because the person is abandoning the clear obligation (Friday) which is stronger than Zuhr. According to Zufar and the three other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali), such Zuhr prayer is actually invalid. The Hanafi school argues that the original obligation is Zuhr (since Friday is not obligatory on him alone if he cannot meet its conditions), but he is commanded to drop Zuhr by attending Friday. Thus, by praying Zuhr first, he is sinning, but the prayer is valid (though prohibited). Second, if after praying Zuhr he then proceeds to the Friday prayer (e.g., leaves his house when the imam is already in prayer), his earlier Zuhr prayer becomes invalid (batil) and turns into a nafl (voluntary) prayer. This rule applies to both the excused and unexcused, according to the madhhab. The commentator notes that the term 'fasad' would be more appropriate than 'butlan'.

Key Terms
كره تحريماً (kariha tahrīman): Disliked in the sense of prohibition; forbidden (haram) but slightly less severe than absolute haram.
سعى إليها (sa‘ā ilayhā): Proceeded to the Friday prayer after having already prayed Zuhr, by leaving his house and heading to the mosque.
بطل (batala): Became invalid; here it means the Zuhr prayer becomes void and is transformed into a voluntary prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) His Zuhr becomes invalid and turns into a voluntary prayer.
C) His Zuhr is valid but he must repeat Zuhr after Friday.
D) He has committed a sin but his Zuhr remains valid.

Key Takeaway
For the unexcused, praying Zuhr before Friday is valid but sinful; if one then proceeds to Friday, the Zuhr turns into a voluntary prayer.

Zuhr in Congregation on Friday: Nafl, Not Invalid
Ruling on Zuhr congregation in city and catching imam in tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday in a city and explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding when it becomes nafl.

Core Idea
Zuhr in congregation on Friday in a city becomes nafl, not invalid.

The obligation of Jumu'ah supersedes Zuhr on Friday. The Hanafi school, however, does not declare Zuhr invalid if one prays it in congregation; rather, it transforms into a supererogatory act. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the wisdom behind it, and the differences among the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Base Ruling
The base text rules that performing Zuhr in congregation in a city (misr) on Friday turns into nafl, not invalid. Determine what triggers this transformation.
The act is deliberate Zuhr in jama'ah; solitary Zuhr may be treated differently.
2
Understand the Rationale
The commentary explains that this prevents reduction of the Jumu'ah congregation and avoids a conflicting form of Jumu'ah by performing another prayer.
The 'illa (effective cause) is the protection of Jumu'ah congregation.
3
Trace the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds it becomes nafl in all cases. Sahibayn limit it to when one catches the imam. Zufar excludes the excused person. Identify each position.
This difference has practical consequences for travel, slavery, and catching the imam.
4
Examine the Dalil
The hadith 'Whatever you catch, pray; whatever you miss, complete' is cited by the Sahibayn. Understand how it is interpreted differently.
The Hanafi response is that 'complete' refers to finishing the imam's prayer, not starting a new one.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The text states 'ala al-qawl bih' (the relied-upon view), which is that the latecomer completes as Jumu'ah if he catches the imam. For the main ruling, Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi.
Know the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة الجمعة أداء الظهر بجماعة في المصر، ومن أدركها في التشهد أو سجود السهو أتم جمعة على القول به في الجمعة أي هذا المدرك يوم الجمعة وكذا بأذان وإقامة أي الجمعة حال كون الإمام سم س م وإذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا كلام، = المعنى المطلوب من كل وجه والفساد ما يفوت المعنى المطلوب من وجه دون وجه والظهر هنا لم تبطل من كل وجه، بل انقلب نفلاً، سواء كان أدرك الإمام فيها أو لا، وسواء كان معذوراً كالمسافر والعبد أو لا، وقالا: إن لم يدرك الإمام لا يبطل، وقال زفر: لا يبطل ظهر المعذور، فإن خرج من بيته والإمام فرغ منها لا يبطل إجماعاً؛ لأن شرط بطلانها بالسعي عند الإمام خروجه من بيته قبل شروع الإمام بعده، وإن خرج من بيته والإمام فيها، فقبل أن يصل إليه فرغ منها بطل عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما، وإن خرج لا يقصد الجمعة لم تبطل إجماعاً. (فتح) أداء الظهر إلخ لأنها تفضي إلى تقليل جماعة الجمعة؛ لأنه ربما يتطرق غير المعذور للاقتداء بالمعذور، ولأن فيه صورة عارضة للجمعة بإقامة غيرها بخلاف القرية، فإنه ليس فيها جمعة، فلا تفضي إلى التقليل ولا إلى المعارضة. (فتح، مسكين) في المصر: سواء كان قبل فراغ الإمام أو بعده يروى ذلك عن علي الله ولا يكره في القرية. (ط،ع) أتم جمعة: وقال محمد: إن أدرك أكثر الركعة الثانية مع الإمام أتم جمعة وإن أدرك أقلها أتم ظهراً؛ لأنه جمعة من وجه وظهر من وجه؛ لفوات بعض الشروط في حقه فيصلي أربعاً اعتباراً للظهر، ويقعد على رأس الركعتين لا محالة اعتباراً للجمعة، ولهما: قوله عليه: "فما أدركتم فصلوا وما فاتكم فاقضوا"، أمر بقضاء ما فاته، وهو الذي صلى الإمام قبل الاقتداء به لا صلاة أخرى غير الجمعة رمز الحقائق: ١٠٠/١]
Chapter of Friday Prayer: Performing Zuhr in congregation in the city, and whoever catches it in tashahhud or sujud al-sahw completes it as Friday prayer according to the relied-upon view in Friday prayer, i.e., this latecomer on Friday, and likewise with adhan and iqama, i.e., the Friday prayer when the imam is [present] ... and when the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech. = The intended meaning from every aspect and corruption is what loses the intended meaning from one aspect without another, and here the Zuhr does not become invalid from every aspect, but rather turns into a supererogatory prayer, whether he caught the imam in it or not, and whether he is excused like a traveler or slave or not. The two companions said: If he did not catch the imam, it does not become invalid. Zufar said: The Zuhr of the excused person does not become invalid. If he left his house and the imam had finished it, it does not become invalid by consensus because the condition for its invalidation by hastening according to the imam is his leaving his house before the imam starts after him. If he left his house and the imam is in it, and he reached him after he finished, it becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa contrary to them. If he left not intending the Friday prayer, it does not become invalid by consensus. (Fath) The performance of Zuhr etc. because it leads to reducing the congregation of Friday prayer; because perhaps an unexcused person may imitate an excused person, and because it involves a conflicting form of Friday prayer by performing another prayer, unlike the village, for there is no Friday prayer in it, so it does not lead to reduction nor to conflict. (Fath, Miskin) In the city: whether it is before or after the imam finishes, it is narrated from Ali, may God be pleased with him, and it is not disliked in the village. (T, A) He completes Friday prayer: Muhammad said: If he catches most of the second rak'ah with the imam, he completes it as Friday prayer; if he catches less, he completes it as Zuhr because it is Friday from one aspect and Zuhr from another; due to the loss of some conditions in his case, he prays four rak'ahs considering Zuhr, and sits after two rak'ahs necessarily considering Friday. For them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whatever you catch, pray, and whatever you miss, complete', he ordered to make up what he missed, which is what the imam prayed before he joined him, not another prayer other than Friday. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:100)
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the ruling of performing Zuhr prayer in congregation in a city (misr) on Friday. The base text states that if someone prays Zuhr in congregation in a city on Friday, his prayer is not valid as Zuhr but turns into a supererogatory (nafl) prayer, even if he catches the imam of Jumu'ah in the tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw. The commentary explains the reasoning: the prayer does not become invalid entirely (fasid) but rather becomes nafl because the intended obligation (Zuhr) is superseded by the obligation of Jumu'ah. This applies whether the person is excused (like a traveler or slave) or not. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differ: they say if he did not catch the imam, his Zuhr does not become invalid (i.e., it remains valid as Zuhr). Zufar says the Zuhr of an excused person does not become invalid. The commentary then discusses the condition for invalidation: according to Abu Hanifa, if a person leaves his house intending to go to Jumu'ah, his Zuhr becomes invalid only if he leaves before the imam starts the khutbah? Actually, the text says: 'if he leaves his house and the imam is in it (i.e., the prayer), and before he reaches him he finishes, it becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa.' There is also a consensus that if he leaves his house without intending Jumu'ah, his Zuhr does not become invalid. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir explains the wisdom: to prevent reduction of the Jumu'ah congregation and to avoid mixing intentions. Then there is a sub-ruling about catching the imam in the second rak'ah: Muhammad al-Shaybani distinguishes between catching most of the second rak'ah (then he completes as Jumu'ah) vs. less (then he completes as Zuhr). The Sahibayn argue using the hadith 'Whatever you catch, pray, and whatever you miss, complete', which they interpret as making up the missed prayer (i.e., the remainder of the imam's prayer is a separate act, not another prayer). The relied-upon view is that he completes as Jumu'ah if he catches any part of the second rak'ah? The text says 'on the relied-upon view in Friday prayer' meaning the accepted position is that he completes as Friday prayer.

Key Terms
المصر (al-misr): A large city where Friday prayer is established.
أتم جمعة (atamma jumu'ah): Completes it as Friday prayer, meaning his prayer is valid as Jumu'ah and he does not need to pray Zuhr.
نفلاً (naflan): Supererogatory prayer; the Zuhr becomes a voluntary act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what happens to a person who prays Zuhr in congregation in a city on Friday and does not attend Jumu'ah?
A) His prayer is invalid and he must repeat it as Zuhr.
B) His prayer becomes a supererogatory (nafl) prayer, and he must still pray Zuhr if not excused.
C) His prayer is valid as Zuhr if he does not catch the Jumu'ah imam.
D) His prayer is valid as Zuhr only if he is a traveler.

Key Takeaway
Performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday in a city turns it into a supererogatory act; the obligation of Zuhr is not fulfilled and Jumu'ah remains mandatory.
