When the Imam Emerges for Khutbah: The Hanafi Ruling on Prayer and Speech
Ruling on refraining from prayer and speech when imam comes out

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer and speech during the Friday khutbah, identify the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences, and apply the principle that prohibition outweighs command (an-nahi raajihun 'ala al-amr).

Core Idea
When the imam appears for Friday khutbah, all prayer and speech are prohibited — even acts of worship like Sunnah and greeting the mosque.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a critical fiqh issue: what happens when the imam steps out for the Friday sermon? Abu Hanifa's position is absolute — no prayer, no speech — while his students and later scholars nuance the ruling. Moreover, the Shafi'i school permits certain prayers and greetings. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh conflicting evidence, especially when a general prohibition contradicts a command to perform an act of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling and its scope
Determine what exactly is prohibited: prayer (all types) and speech (worldly and religious). Note the condition: when the imam appears (emerges) for the khutbah.
The prohibition lasts until the imam finishes the sermon.
2
Trace the evidence: the hadith 'When the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech'
Examine the hadith as a general (amm) text. Understand why Hanafis consider it binding without exception.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but still authoritative.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference
Compare Abu Hanifa's absolute view with the Sahibayn's distinction between speech before/after the sermon and prayer. Note also the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on speech during the preacher's silence.
The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa's absolute prohibition.
4
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i
Identify the Shafi'i position that allows Sunnah, greeting of the mosque, and returning salaam. Understand their dalil: commands to perform these acts.
The Hanafi response uses the principle that an-nahi raajihun 'ala al-amr (prohibition outweighs command).
5
Understand the Hanafi principle: prohibition outweighs command
Learn how the Hanafi school resolves conflict between a general prohibition (nahi) and specific commands (amr). The prohibition is given precedence because it is general and the commands are exceptions that do not apply here.
This principle is used in many fiqh disputes beyond this case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا خرج إلخ أي إذا ظهر الإمام يوم الجمعة ترك الناس الصلاة والكلام حتى يفرغ من خطبته، هذا عند أبي حنيفة : لقوله : "إذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة ولا كلام" من غير فصل وقالا لا بأس بالكلام إذا خرج الإمام قبل أن يخطب، وإذا نزل قبل أن يكبر؛ لأن الكراهة الاختلال بفرض الاستماع، ولا استماع ههنا بخلاف الصلاة؛ لأنها قد تمتد إلى حالة الخطبة وله ما روينا ولأن الكلام أيضاً قد يمتد طبعاً، فأشبه الصلاة، فما يؤدي إلى الحرام فهو حرام. (مستخلص) فلأنه وقال الشافعي: يأتي بالسنة وتحية المسجد ويرد السلام؛ لأن الأوليين مأمور بهما عن الشارع عليه، وأما رد السلام، واجب لا يجوز تركه، قلنا: هذا من المواضع المستثناة من الوجوب، وأمره علي معارض بقوله عليه: "إذا خرج الإمام" الحديث من غير فصل؛ لأنه بإطلاقه شامل للسنة وتحية المسجد، والأخذ به أولى؛ لأن النهي راجح على الأمر، على أن الحديث محمول على ما قبل المنع والمراد بالكلام الذي يتعلق بالآخرة، أما غيره فيكره إجماعاً، واختلف في إباحة الكلام في جلسة الخطيب وسكوته، فأباحه أبو يوسف ومنعه محمد. (فتح) الإمام من الحجرة إن كان فيها أو قام المصعود إن لم يكن فيها. (ط) ولا كلام: مطلقاً سواء خطب أو لم يخطب. (مسكين)
"And when the imam comes out" etc.: That is, when the imam appears on Friday, people abandon prayer and speech until he finishes his sermon. This is according to Abu Hanifa, based on his saying: "When the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech" without distinction. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: There is no harm in speech when the imam comes out before he begins the sermon, and when he descends before the takbir, because the dislike is due to disrupting the obligation of listening, and there is no listening here, unlike prayer, because it may extend to the time of the sermon. And he has what we narrated, and because speech may also extend naturally, so it resembles prayer. That which leads to the forbidden is forbidden. (Mustakhlas) [...] Al-Shafi'i said: One should perform the Sunnah prayer and the greeting of the mosque and return the greeting, because the first two are commanded by the Lawgiver, and returning the greeting is obligatory and not permissible to abandon. We say: This is one of the exceptional cases where the obligation is removed, and his command is contradicted by his saying, peace be upon him: "When the imam comes out" hadith without distinction, because it generally includes the Sunnah and the greeting of the mosque. And adopting it is better because the prohibition outweighs the command. Moreover, the hadith is interpreted as applying before the prohibition, and the meaning of speech is that which pertains to the Hereafter. As for other than that, it is disliked by consensus. And there is a disagreement about the permissibility of speech during the sitting and silence of the preacher: Abu Yusuf permitted it, Muhammad forbade it. (Fath) The imam [comes out] from the room if he is in it, or he ascends the pulpit if not. (T) And no speech: absolutely, whether he is delivering the sermon or not. (Miskin)
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when the imam comes out for the Friday sermon. The base text states that when the imam emerges, there is to be no prayer and no speech. Abu Hanifa holds this prohibition applies unconditionally from the moment the imam appears until the end of the sermon. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) differentiate: they say speech before the imam begins to deliver the sermon is not prohibited, and similarly after he descends before the takbir, because the reason for prohibition is the obligation to listen, which only occurs during the sermon itself. However, prayer is prohibited at all times because it might extend into the sermon. The text then addresses Imam al-Shafi'i's view, who permits the Sunnah prayer, mosque greeting, and responding to greetings, arguing they are commanded or obligatory. The Hanafi response is that this is an exceptional case where the command to pray is superseded by the prohibition in the hadith 'When the imam comes out, there is no prayer and no speech.' The prohibition is general and takes precedence over commands, and the hadith is interpreted as covering even acts of worship that could disrupt the sermon. There is also a difference among the Hanafi school regarding speech during the preacher's sitting: Abu Yusuf permits it, Muhammad forbids it. The relied-upon view is that all speech and prayer are prohibited during the khutbah.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam on Friday before the prayer.
لا صلاة ولا كلام (la salata wa la kalam): No prayer and no speech—prohibition of any prayer (including Sunnah) and any worldly or religious speech during the khutbah.
النهي راجح على الأمر (an-nahi raajihun 'ala al-amr): The principle that a prohibition (nahi) outweighs a command (amr) when they conflict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does the prohibition of prayer and speech begin on Friday?
A) From the beginning of the khutbah.
B) From the moment the imam appears (emerges) for the khutbah.
C) Only when the imam starts speaking.
D) From the time the adhan is called.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits any prayer or speech from the moment the imam appears for the Friday khutbah, based on the general hadith and the principle that prohibition outweighs command.

Obligation of Sa'ee and Prohibition of Sale at the First Adhan
Ruling on hastening to Jumu'ah and forbidding sale at first adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sa'ee and sale during the first adhan of Jumu'ah, explain the Quranic evidence, and distinguish between the intra-Hanafi views on which adhan triggers the obligation.

Core Idea
The first adhan triggers a double obligation: hasten to prayer and cease trade.

The Friday prayer is one of the most distinguished communal obligations in Islam. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the twin rulings that take effect at the first adhan: the obligation to hasten (sa'ee) to the mosque and the prohibition of buying and selling. The primary evidence is the divine command in Surah al-Jumu'ah, but later scholars debated precisely which adhan (first or second) triggers these rulings. Understanding this debate reveals both the depth of Hanafi usul and the practical implications for daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the twin rulings
Extract the two distinct obligations at the time of the adhan: (1) sa'ee – hastening to the mosque for Jumu'ah; (2) abandoning sale – ceasing all trade transactions.
These are separate wajibat, not just recommendations.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The passage cites Quran 62:9 – identify the verse and note that it is the basis for both rulings. Recognize that the verse is qati al-thubut but zanni al-dalala due to differing interpretations of 'al-nida'.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'fas'aw' indicates wujub. Similarly, 'dharu al-bay' indicates prohibition. Understand why this derivation is strong yet open to ikhtilaf.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Three views are mentioned: (a) the first adhan after zawal (most correct); (b) the second adhan at the minbar; (c) the entry of time even without adhan. Al-Hasan's narration from Abu Hanifa considers the adhan on the minaret (second adhan) as the criterion.
The text says 'al-asahh' (most correct) for the first adhan after zawal, which is the mufta bihi.
5
Examine the cross-madhhab difference on sale
The passage concludes that a sale concluded during the adhan time is valid but makruh tahrimi, contrary to some Shafi'is and Hanbalis who consider it invalid. Note the practical consequence: the contract is not void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب السعي وترك البيع بالأذان الأول، فإن جلس على المنبر أذن بين يديه، على من عليه الجمعة إلى الجمعة بعد تمام الخطبة وأقيم بإقامة الجمعة أي الإمام يعني أذن المؤذن بالأذان الأول: [الواقع بعد الزوال في الأصح. (ط)] وقيل: يجب السعي بالأذان الثاني أي عند المنبر؛ لأنه لم يكن في زمن النبي إلا هو، وكذا في عهد أبي بكر وعمر لها وزاد عثمان اهله الله الأذان على الزوراء أي المكان المرتفع، وقيل: يجب بدخول الوقت وإن لم يؤذن لها أحد، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن المعتبر في وجوب السعي وحرمة البيع الأذان على المنارة، والأصل في ذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿إِذَا نُودِيَ لِلصَّلاةِ مِنْ فِ مِنْ يَوْمِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللَّهِ وَذَرُوا الْبَيْعَ (الجمعة:٩) ثم إذا عقد البيع وقت الأذان ينعقد، ولكنه يكره خلافاً لبعض الشافعية والحنابلة رمز الحقائق: ۱۰۰/۱](مستخلص) أذن إلخ بالبناء للمفعول ولا يستعمل مبنياً للفاعل، وقوله: "بين يديه" أي بين يدي الخطيب، وأفاد بوحدة الفعل أن المؤذن إن كان أكثر من واحد أذنوا واحداً بعد واحد يعني إذا اتسع المسجد وكثر الجماعات بحيث أن صوت المؤذن وحده لا يبلغ جميعهم واحتيج إلى اجتماع المؤذنين في الأذان لا يجتمعون، بل يؤذنون واحدا بعد واحد بأن يجعل كل مؤذن في ناحية من نواحي المسجد. (فتح)
And it is obligatory to hasten (sa'ee) and to abandon sale with the first adhan. Then when he sits on the minbar, he (the mu'adhdhin) calls the adhan at his hands, upon those who are obliged to Friday prayer, to go to Friday after the completion of the sermon, and the iqama is established for the Friday prayer i.e., the imam means the mu'adhdhin calls the first adhan: [which takes place after zawal (noon) according to the most correct view (T)]. And it is said that sa'ee is obligatory with the second adhan, i.e., at the minbar, because in the time of the Prophet there was only one adhan, and likewise in the time of Abu Bakr and Umar, may God be pleased with them, and Uthman increased the adhan on al-Zawra', meaning the raised place. And it is said that it is obligatory with the entry of time even if no one calls the adhan. Al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa that what is considered for the obligation of sa'ee and the prohibition of sale is the adhan on the minaret. The basis for this is the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'When the call is made for the prayer on the day of Friday, then hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade' (Al-Jumu'ah:9). Then if a sale is concluded at the time of the adhan, it is valid, but it is disliked, contrary to some Shafi'is and Hanbalis (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:100) (Mustakhlas). 'Adhan' etc. is in the passive voice and not used in the active. His saying 'at his hands' means in front of the preacher. And the singularity of the action indicates that if there is more than one mu'adhdhin, they call one after another, i.e., if the mosque is large and the congregations are numerous such that the voice of one mu'adhdhin alone does not reach them all, and there is need for multiple mu'adhdhins to be together in the adhan, they do not recite together, but recite one after another, with each mu'adhdhin placed in a corner of the mosque. (Fath)
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on hastening (sa'ee) to Jumu'ah and the prohibition of trade at the time of the first adhan. The base text states that when the imam sits on the minbar, the adhan is called in front of him, and it becomes wajib for those obligated to attend Jumu'ah to hasten and stop selling. There is a difference of opinion: the most correct view is that the obligation is triggered by the first adhan after zawal (noon), but some say it is the second adhan at the minbar (historical practice until Uthman added a second). Another view is that the obligation begins with the entry of time, even without an adhan. Al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa that the adhan on the minaret is the criterion. The primary evidence is Quran 62:9 'When the call is made for the prayer on Friday, hasten to the remembrance of Allah and leave off trade.' A sale concluded at the time of the adhan is valid but makruh (disliked), contrary to some Shafi'is and Hanbalis who consider it batil. The passage also addresses the practical situation when there are multiple mu'adhdhins in a large mosque: they should call the adhan one after another, not simultaneously, to ensure it reaches all corners.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'ee): Hastening to go to the Friday prayer after the adhan is called.
الأذان الأول (al-adhan al-awwal): The first call to prayer for Jumu'ah, which occurs after zawal (noon) according to the correct view.
البيع (al-bay'): Sale or trade transaction, which is prohibited during the time of the adhan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct Hanafi view, when does the obligation to hasten to Jumu'ah (sa'ee) become binding?
A) At the second adhan at the minbar.
B) At the first adhan after zawal.
C) As soon as the time for Zuhr enters.
D) Only when the imam sits on the minbar.

Key Takeaway
The first adhan of Jumu'ah triggers the wajib of hastening to prayer and the prohibition of trade, with the sale remaining valid but disliked – a distinctive Hanafi position.

Recommended Acts Before Friday Prayer and During Khutbah
List of mustahabbat for Friday prayer and khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least five recommended acts for Friday prayer and explain the correct sitting posture during the khutbah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Friday prayer is enhanced by recommended acts of grooming, early arrival, and respectful sitting during the sermon.

This lesson focuses on the sunan (recommended acts) for Friday prayer that are not obligatory but highly meritorious. The passage details personal preparations like applying perfume and wearing white clothes, as well as conduct during the khutbah such as sitting like tashahhud. Understanding these practices helps a Muslim perfect his Friday observance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
Scan the passage and list each act described as mustahabb or appropriate for Friday. These include applying oil, perfume, wearing best and white clothes, sitting in tashahhud posture, early arrival, and sitting in the first row.
The imam's recitation is also addressed.
2
Categorize the acts by type
Group the acts into personal grooming (oil, perfume, clothes) and conduct (sitting posture, early arrival, front row). This helps see the breadth of sunan.
3
Note the nuance on the imam's recitation
The imam should recite in Jumu'ah like Zuhr (moderate length). Reciting specific reported surahs is good but should not become a persistent practice that might be mistaken for obligatory.
This prevents innovation.
4
Understand the sitting posture
The preferred posture during the khutbah is sitting as in tashahhud (resting squarely on the hips with hands on thighs). The passage also permits ihtiba' (hugging shins) as an alternative.
Some schools may dislike ihtiba', but Hanafis allow it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة: لم يذكر المصنف الأمور المستحبة يوم الجمعة كما ذكرها في صلاة العيد فلنذكر شيئاً منها، فالمستحب لمن أراد حضور الجمعة أن يدهن وأن يمس طيبا، وأن يلبس أحسن ثيابه وأن تكون بيضا، وأن يقعد عند استماع الخطبة كما يقعد في التشهد ولا بأس بالاحتباء، وينبغي للإمام أن يقرأ فيها كالظهر، ولو قرأ تبركا بالسور المأثورة كان حسنا إن لم يواظب عليه، وأن يتبكر، وأن يجلس في الصف الأول إن قدر وهو ما يلي الإمام، ثم اعلم أنهم اختلفوا في جواز السؤال في المسجد وفي جواز الدفع إليه والمختار أن السائل إن كان لا يمر بين يدي المصلي ولا يتخطى رقاب الناس، ولا يسأل إلحافاً بل لأمر لابد منه، فلا بأس بالسؤال، والدفع إليه، ولا بأس الجمعة إذا خرج من عمران المصر قبل دخول وقت الظهر، والصحيح أنه يكره السفر بعد الزوال قبل بالسفر يوم أن يصليها. ولا يكره قبل الزوال. (فتح) بين يديه أي بين يدي المنبر، بذلك جرى التوارث، ولا ينبغي أن يصلي غير الخطيب؛ لأن القصر للخطبة فلا يقيمهما اثنان [ رمز الحقائق (١٠١/١] تمام الخطبة والفصل بينهما بأمر الدنيا مكروه.
Supplement: The author did not mention the recommended acts on Friday as he mentioned them in the Eid prayer, so we will mention some of them: It is recommended for the one who wants to attend Friday prayer to apply oil, apply perfume, wear his best clothes and have them be white, and sit while listening to the sermon as he sits in tashahhud, and there is no harm in sitting in ihtiba' posture. It is appropriate for the imam to recite in it (the prayer) like Zuhr, and if he recites for blessing with the reported surahs, it is good as long as he does not persist. And he should go early, and sit in the first row if possible, which is the one next to the imam. Then know that they differed on the permissibility of asking in the mosque and giving to the asker. The chosen view is that if the asker is not passing in front of the worshippers or stepping over people's necks, and does not ask persistently, but for a necessary matter, then there is no harm in asking and giving. And there is no harm in traveling on Friday if he leaves the built-up area of the city before the entry of Zuhr time, and the correct view is that it is disliked to travel after zawal before he prays it, and it is not disliked before zawal. (Fath) 'At his hands' means in front of the minbar, and this is the inherited practice. It is not appropriate for anyone other than the preacher to pray, because the restriction is for the sermon, so it should not be performed by two people (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:101). The complete sermon and separation by worldly matters between them is disliked.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This supplement (tatimah) lists the recommended acts (mustahabbat) for Friday prayer, which the author of the matn had not included. These include: applying oil and perfume, wearing the best clothes (preferably white), sitting in a manner similar to tashahhud while listening to the khutbah (ihtiba' posture is permitted). The imam is recommended to recite in Jumu'ah similar to Zuhr (i.e., not too long), but if he recites the reported surahs for blessing it is good, as long as he does not make it a habit. Going early and sitting in the first row (next to the imam) is also recommended. The passage also addresses the issue of asking (begging) in the mosque: the chosen view is that it is permissible if the asker does not disturb worshippers and has a genuine need. Regarding traveling on Friday, it is not disliked to travel before zawal, but it is disliked to travel after zawal before having prayed Jumu'ah. Finally, it mentions that the adhan at the minbar should be performed by the mu'adhdhin, and it is not appropriate for anyone other than the preacher to lead the prayer; also, separating the two parts of the sermon with worldly talk is disliked.

Key Terms
المستحب (al-mustahabb): Recommended acts for Friday prayer that are not obligatory.
الاحتباء (al-ihtiba'): Sitting on the buttocks with legs drawn up and shins hugged to the chest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT recommended for Friday prayer?
A) Applying oil.
B) Wearing white clothes.
C) Using a miswak.
D) Sitting in the first row.

Key Takeaway
Friday prayer is preceded by sunan of personal grooming and early arrival; listening to the khutbah should be done in a reverent posture like tashahhud, with ihtiba' permitted.

Rulings on Asking for Charity in the Mosque
Ruling on asking in the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the conditions under which asking for charity in the mosque is permissible according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Begging in the mosque is permissible only if it does not disturb worship and is for genuine need.

This lesson addresses the permissibility of asking for charity in the mosque. The Hanafi school permits it under specific conditions to prevent disruption and harassment, balancing compassion with respect for the sacred space.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disagreement
Note that scholars differed on the permissibility of asking in the mosque. The passage presents the chosen view (mukhtar) of the Hanafi school.
2
State the chosen view
The Hanafi school permits both asking and giving in the mosque if conditions are met.
3
List the conditions
The passage specifies three conditions: (1) the asker must not pass in front of those praying, (2) he must not step over people's necks, and (3) he must not ask persistently (ilḥāf). Additionally, the asker should have a genuine need (لأمر لابد منه).
These conditions protect the worship and dignity of others.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a person who quietly asks individuals after the prayer ends, without blocking or disturbing. This is permissible.

Rulings on Traveling on Friday
Ruling on traveling on Friday

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when traveling on Friday is permissible, disliked, or permissible according to the Hanafi school based on the time of departure.

Core Idea
Travel on Friday is permissible before zawal, but after zawal it is disliked unless one has prayed Jumu'ah first.

Many people plan trips on Fridays. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on traveling on Friday, differentiating between departure before and after the entry of Zuhr time (zawal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for leaving before Zuhr time
The passage says there is no harm (لا بأس) in traveling if one leaves the built-up area before the entry of Zuhr time.
This means it is permissible and not disliked.
2
Identify the ruling for leaving after zawal
After zawal (i.e., after the beginning of Zuhr time), it is disliked (يكره) to travel before performing the Friday prayer (قبل أن يصليها).
The dislike is tanzihi (slightly disliked).
3
Note the exception: if one prays first
If one prays the Friday prayer first, there is no dislike in traveling afterwards.
The dislike is specifically for avoiding the prayer.
4
Understand 'built-up area'
'عمران المصر' refers to the built-up area of the city. Leaving this before Zuhr time is the condition.
If one lives within the city limits, this applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And he should go early, and sit in the first row if possible, which is the one next to the imam. Then know that they differed on the permissibility of asking in the mosque and giving to the asker. The chosen view is that if the asker is not passing in front of the worshippers or stepping over people's necks, and does not ask persistently, but for a necessary matter, then there is no harm in asking and giving. And there is no harm in traveling on Friday if he leaves the built-up area of the city before the entry of Zuhr time, and the correct view is that it is disliked to travel after zawal before he prays it, and it is not disliked before zawal. (Fath) 'At his hands' means in front of the minbar, and this is the inherited practice. It is not appropriate for anyone other than the preacher to pray, because the restriction is for the sermon, so it should not be performed by two people (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1:101). The complete sermon and separation by worldly matters between them is disliked.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This supplement (tatimah) lists the recommended acts (mustahabbat) for Friday prayer, which the author of the matn had not included. These include: applying oil and perfume, wearing the best clothes (preferably white), sitting in a manner similar to tashahhud while listening to the khutbah (ihtiba' posture is permitted). The imam is recommended to recite in Jumu'ah similar to Zuhr (i.e., not too long), but if he recites the reported surahs for blessing it is good, as long as he does not make it a habit. Going early and sitting in the first row (next to the imam) is also recommended. The passage also addresses the issue of asking (begging) in the mosque: the chosen view is that it is permissible if the asker does not disturb worshippers and has a genuine need. Regarding traveling on Friday, it is not disliked to travel before zawal, but it is disliked to travel after zawal before having prayed Jumu'ah. Finally, it mentions that the adhan at the minbar should be performed by the mu'adhdhin, and it is not appropriate for anyone other than the preacher to lead the prayer; also, separating the two parts of the sermon with worldly talk is disliked.

Key Terms
الزوال (al-zawāl): The moment when the sun passes its zenith, marking the beginning of Zuhr time.
عمران المصر (ʻimrān al-miṣr): The built-up area of a city (the urban zone).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it disliked to travel on Friday?
A) Before zawal.
B) After zawal without having prayed Jumu'ah.
C) After praying Jumu'ah.
D) At any time on Friday.

Key Takeaway
Travel on Friday is permissible before the start of Zuhr time; after that, it is disliked unless you pray Jumu'ah first.

Adhan Placement, Preacher's Role, and Sermon Integrity on Friday
Rulings on adhan, preacher, and sermon content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state where the adhan is given on Friday, who should lead the prayer, and the ruling on inserting worldly matters between the two parts of the sermon.

Core Idea
The adhan is delivered at the minbar, only the preacher leads the prayer, and worldly talk between sermon parts is disliked.

This lesson covers three practical aspects of the Friday service: the physical placement of the second adhan, the restriction on who may lead the prayer, and the prohibition of interjecting worldly topics during the sermon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the adhan location
The passage states that the adhan is given 'at his hands' meaning in front of the minbar. This is the inherited practice (التوارث).
This is specific to the adhan during the khutbah.
2
Determine who should lead the prayer
It is not appropriate (لا ينبغي) for anyone other than the khatib (preacher) to lead the prayer, because the restriction (القصر) is for the sermon.
The sermon and prayer are connected; the same person should deliver both.
3
Understand the ruling on separation by worldly matters
Separating the two parts of the sermon with worldly talk (الفصل بينهما بأمر الدنيا) is disliked (مكروه).
This includes announcements about lost items, business, etc.

Salah — Prayer

Eid Prayer: Obligation, Conditions, and Recommended Acts
Ruling on obligation of Eid prayer and its conditions, with recommended eating of dates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Eid prayer as wajib, list its three categories of conditions (obligation, performance, validity), and apply the recommended eating of dates before Eid al-Fitr.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib on those qualified for Jumu'ah, but khutbah is not a condition.

Eid prayer is one of the most visible acts of worship in the Islamic calendar. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes its legal status, clarifies who must attend, and distinguishes between conditions that make it obligatory, conditions for proper performance, and conditions for validity. It also addresses a beloved Sunnah: eating dates before the 'Id al-Fitr prayer. Understanding these layers prevents common mistakes, such as assuming khutbah is a requirement for Eid or that the prayer is merely recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and basis for obligation
Locate the opening statement that Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) and note the key conditions: it applies to those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, excluding khutbah. Understand that 'wajib' here means a confirmed obligation (wajib mu'akkad), not fard.
The text uses 'tajib' (obligatory), and later clarifies the dispute.
2
Locate the dalil from Quran and Sunnah
Find the evidence cited: verse 'fasalli li rabbika wanhar' (Al-Kawthar:2) and 'wa litukabbiru' (Al-Baqarah:185), plus the Prophet's continuous practice. Note that for Hanafis, a command (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a contrary indicator.
These proofs are zanni al-dalala, hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
3
Understand the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
Identify the contrasting views: Shafi'i and Maliki consider it sunnah mu'akkadah; Ahmad ibn Hanbal considers it fard kifayah. The Hanafi response relies on the strength of the continuous practice and the command.
The text mentions 'al-mukhtar 'inda al-jumhur' (the chosen view of the majority) to establish tarjih.
4
Distinguish the three categories of conditions
The passage breaks down conditions into: (a) conditions of obligation (shurut al-wujub): free, resident, healthy, male, sound sight, ability to walk; (b) conditions of performance (shurut al-ada'): city, sultan, congregation; (c) conditions of validity (shurut al-jawaz): purity, covering awrah, facing qibla, time, intention. Note that khutbah is explicitly excluded from conditions of performance.
This tripartite division is typical in Hanafi fiqh for acts of worship.
5
Apply the recommended eating before Eid al-Fitr
Read the final section: it is mustahabb (recommended) to eat an odd number of dates (three, five, etc.) before leaving for the musalla. If dates are unavailable, other sweets may be used. The text warns against innovations such as mixing dates with milk without a basis in Sunnah.
This practice is specific to Eid al-Fitr, not Eid al-Adha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة العيدين أي في بيان أحكامها باب صلاة العيدين تجب صلاة العيد على من تجب عليه الجمعة بشرائطها سوى الخطبة، وندب في الفطر أن يطعم أي عيد الفطر أي بشرائط الجمعة أي استحب باب صلاة العيدين المناسبة بين البابين أن الجمعة عيد؛ لقوله عليه: "إن" لكل مؤمن في كل شهر أربعة أعياد أو خمسة"، أو لاشتراكهما في الشروط المتقدمة سوى الخطبة، أو لأنهما يؤديان بجمع عظيم نهاراً، ويجهر فيهما بالقراءة، أو لوجوبها على من تجب عليه الجمعة. وقدمت الجمعة؛ للفرضية، أو لكثرة وقوعها، أو لثبوتها بالكتاب. وأصل العيد عود قلبت الواو ياء لسكونها وانكسار ما قبلها، سمي به؛ لأنه يعود كل سنة، ويجمع على أعياد ليفرق عن أعواد جمع عود يعني آلة اللهو والعود بمعنى الخشبة يجمع على عيدان وصلاة العيدين وغيرها كتكبير التشريق ما شرعت في السنة الأولى من الهجرة كما رواه أبو داود مسنداً إلى أنس له، قال: قدم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم المدينة ولهم يومان يلعبون فيهما فقال: "ما هذان اليومان؟ قالوا: كنا نلعب فيهما في الجاهلية، فقال عليه: "إن الله أبدلكم بهما خيراً منهما يوم الأضحى، ويوم الفطر". (فتح) تجب صلاة العيد عند الجمهور وهو الصحيح وقيل ،تسن وبه قال الشافعي ومالك، وعن أحمد فرض كفاية. (ع)] لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَانْحَرْ﴾ المراد به صلاة العيد، وكذا المراد بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ﴾ (البقرة : ١٨٥) في تأويل، وقد واظب عليها عليه من غير ترك، وهو دليل الوجوب، وهذا رواية الحسن عن الإمام، وهو المختار عند الجمهور، وذكر في الجامع الصغير: عيدان إذا اجتمعا في يوم واحد فالأول سنة والثاني فريضة، ولا يترك واحد منهما، ووجه سنيتها: قوله عليه في حديث الأعرابي عقيب سؤاله: هل علي غيرهن، قال: "لا، إلا أن تطوع، والأول أصح، وتسميتها بالسنة للوجوب بالسنة. (فتح، مستخلص) على من تجب اعلم أن لها شرائط للأداء، وشرائط للوجوب، وشرائط للجواز، فبقوله: "على من تجب" بين شرائط الوجوب أي الحر المقيم الصحيح المذكر مع سلامة البصر وقدرة المشي، وبين شرائط الأداء بقوله: "بشرائطها سوى الخطبة" وهي المصر، والسلطان والجماعة، وشروط الجواز هي: الطهارة، وستر العورة، واستقبال القبلة، والوقت، والنية. والخطبة ليست من شرائطها؛ لأنها تؤدى بعد الصلاة، وشرط الشيء يسبقه، أو يقارنه. (فتح) الجمعة: فلا تجب على المسافر والعبد وإن أذن له ،مولاه، والمريض، والمرأة. (ع) بشرائطها: أي بشرائط الجمعة من شروط الأداء، والجواز. (ع) سوى الخطبة فإنها ليست بشرط في العيد بخلاف الجمعة [رمز الحقائق: ۱۰۱/۱] أن يطعم وما يفعله الناس في زماننا من جمع التمر مع اللبن والفطر عليه فليس له أصل في السنة، وما قيل من التخيير بين التمر وغيره مما هو حلو فيه تأمل، وينبغي أن لا يعدل عن التمر إلى غيره عند وجوده؛ لأنه المأثور كما أنه عليها لا يغدو يوم الفطر حتى يأكل تمرات وتراً. أن يطعم بفتح الياء والعين أي يأكل قبل الخروج إلى المصلى تميرات ثلاثاً، أو خمساً، وأن يكون وتراً، وشيئاً من أي حلو كان بذلك ورد الأثر. [رمز الحقائق: ١٠١/١] روي ا:
The Chapter of the Two Eid Prayers, i.e., explaining their rulings. The Chapter of the Two Eid Prayers. The Eid prayer is obligatory upon the one upon whom Friday prayer is obligatory, with its conditions except the khutbah. And it is recommended (mndub) during Fitr to feed, i.e., Eid al-Fitr, i.e., with the conditions of Friday prayer, i.e., recommended. The Chapter of the Two Eid Prayers: The connection between the two chapters is that Friday is a celebration; due to his saying: 'For every believer there are four or five celebrations every month', or due to their sharing in the aforementioned conditions except the khutbah, or because both are performed with a large congregation during the day and the recitation is aloud, or due to its obligation upon whom Friday is obligatory. Friday is given precedence due to its being fard, or because it occurs more frequently, or because it is established by the Book. The root of 'Eid' is 'awd'; the waw is changed to ya because of sukun and the kasra before it. It is called 'Eid' because it returns every year. Its plural is 'a'yad' to distinguish it from 'a'wad', plural of 'ud' meaning a musical instrument, while 'ud' meaning wood has plural 'idan'. The Eid prayer and other acts like takbir of tashriq were legislated in the first year of hijra, as narrated by Abu Dawud in a marfu' hadith from Anas: The Prophet entered Medina and they had two days of play; he said 'What are these two days?' They said 'We used to play during them in Jahiliyyah.' He said 'Allah has replaced them with two better days: the day of Adha and the day of Fitr.' (Fath) The Eid prayer is obligatory according to the majority, and this is the correct view; some say it is sunnah, which is the view of al-Shafi'i and Malik; Ahmad said it is fard kifaya. The evidence is the verse 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice', interpreted as the Eid prayer, and similarly the verse 'And that you magnify Allah for that He has guided you' (al-Baqarah:185). And he consistently performed it without ever leaving it, which is evidence of obligation. This is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam, and it is the chosen view of the majority. It is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir: if two Eids coincide on one day, the first is sunnah and the second is fard, and neither is left. The evidence for it being sunnah is the Prophet's statement in the hadith of the Bedouin after he asked 'Are there any other obligations upon me?' He said 'No, except what you volunteer.' The first view is stronger, and its being called sunnah is due to obligation from the Sunnah. (Fath, Mustakhlas) Upon whom it is obligatory: Know that it has conditions for performance, conditions for obligation, and conditions for validity. By his statement 'upon whom it is obligatory' he explains the conditions of obligation: free, resident, healthy, male, with sound sight and ability to walk. By his statement 'with its conditions except the khutbah' he explains the conditions of performance: the city (misr), the sultan, and congregation. The conditions of validity are: purity, covering the awra, facing the qibla, time, and intention. The khutbah is not among its conditions because it is performed after the prayer, and a condition precedes or accompanies the thing. (Fath) Regarding Friday: It is not obligatory upon the traveler, the slave (even if his master permits), the sick, and the woman. (Ayni) 'With its conditions' means with the conditions of Friday prayer from the conditions of performance and validity. (Ayni) 'Except the khutbah' because it is not a condition in Eid unlike Friday. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 101/1) 'To feed' and what people in our time do of mixing dates with milk and breaking the fast with it has no basis in the Sunnah. As for the idea of choosing between dates and other sweet things, it requires reflection; it is preferable not to turn away from dates to others when they are available because it is the transmitted practice. As he would not go out on the day of Fitr until he ate an odd number of dates. 'To feed' with fatha on the ya and 'ayn means to eat before going out to the musalla: three or five dates, and that it be odd, and anything sweet; that is what has been reported. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 101/1) It is narrated...
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage discusses the Eid prayer. It begins by establishing the obligation of Eid prayer: it is obligatory on the same people upon whom Friday prayer is obligatory, with the same conditions except for the khutbah (which in Eid is delivered after the prayer, while in Friday it is before). The author then provides the rationale for placing this chapter after Friday: Friday is itself a weekly 'Eid', and both involve large daytime congregations with loud recitation. The word 'Eid' derives from 'awd' meaning return, and its plural is 'a'yad'. The Eid prayers were legislated in the first year of Hijra, as per the hadith where the Prophet replaced the pagan festivals with Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha. There is a dispute regarding the ruling: the majority of Hanafis hold it is obligatory (wajib), while Shafi'is and Malikis consider it sunnah, and Ahmad considers it fard kifaya. The Hanafi proof includes the verse 'fasalli li rabbika wanhar' (interpreted as the Eid prayer) and the verse 'wa litukabbiru Allah 'ala ma hadakum', as well as the Prophet's continuous practice. The narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa supports obligation. However, in al-Jami' al-Saghir, if two Eids coincide, the first is called sunnah and the second fard, but neither is left. The description 'sunnah' is due to obligation being derived from the Sunnah. The passage then explains the conditions: conditions of obligation (free, resident, healthy, male, sound sight, ability to walk) and conditions of performance (city, sultan, congregation). It also lists conditions of validity (purity, covering awra, facing qibla, time, intention). The khutbah is not a condition for Eid because it follows the prayer, and a condition must precede or accompany. Friday prayer is not obligatory upon traveler, slave, sick, or woman. Finally, the passage addresses the recommended practice of eating dates before Eid al-Fitr: the Prophet would eat an odd number of dates before going to the musalla. It warns against innovations like mixing dates with milk, and recommends sticking to dates over other sweets if available.

Key Terms
صلاة العيد (salat al-'id): The special prayer performed on the two Eids (al-Fitr and al-Adha); it consists of two rak'ahs with extra takbirs.
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered after the Eid prayer (or before in Friday). In Eid, it is not a condition of the prayer.
التمرات (al-tamarat): Dates; specifically odd numbers of dates (three, five, etc.) eaten before Eid al-Fitr prayer as a recommended practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling of the Eid prayer?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib (obligatory)
C) Fard kifayah
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib on those who meet the conditions of Jumu'ah (free, resident, healthy, male, etc.) but does not require a khutbah for validity, and it is sunnah to eat an odd number of dates before Eid al-Fitr.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Eid Prayer: Its Obligation and Conditions
States the obligation, conditions, and proof of Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer (wajib), identify the three categories of conditions, and explain the proof from Qur'an and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib on the same as Jumu'ah, with distinct conditions for obligation, performance, and validity.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the legal status of the Eid prayer. The author establishes the Hanafi position that it is wajib (obligatory), clarifies who must perform it, and distinguishes between the conditions that trigger obligation, those needed for proper performance, and the general conditions for validity. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Determine the hukm level of Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school. The passage states it is 'wajib' and calls it 'the correct view' despite a minority opinion that it is sunnah.
Contrast with the common misconception that it is merely sunnah even in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the proof
Find the evidence cited: the verse 'fasalli li rabbika wanhar' (Qur'an 108:2) interpreted as referring to Eid prayer, and the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah). Understand how these prove obligation in Hanafi usul.
The amr (imperative) in 'fasalli' indicates wujub per Hanafi principle.
3
Analyze the three categories of conditions
Separate shurut al-wujub (conditions that make it obligatory: free, resident, healthy, male, sight, ability to walk), shurut al-ada' (conditions for performance: city, ruler, congregation), and shurut al-jawaz (conditions for validity: purity, awrah, qiblah, time, intention).
Note that the khutbah is not a condition for Eid because it comes after the prayer.
4
Identify exemptions
List those excused: traveler, slave, sick, woman. Understand why each is exempt based on the conditions of obligation.
The exemption applies to the obligation, not the validity if they choose to attend.
5
Recognize the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
Note that Shafi'i/Maliki hold it is sunnah, Hanbali hold fard kifayah. Compare their proof (hadith of Bedouin) with the Hanafi proof.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is wujub.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة العيدين أي في بيان أحكامها. تجب صلاة العيد على من تجب عليه الجمعة بشرائطها سوى الخطبة. المناسبة بين البابين أن الجمعة عيد؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "إن لكل مؤمن في كل شهر أربعة أعياد أو خمسة"، أو لاشتراكهما في الشروط المتقدمة سوى الخطبة، أو لأنهما يؤديان بجمع عظيم نهاراً، ويجهر فيهما بالقراءة، أو لوجوبها على من تجب عليه الجمعة. وقدمت الجمعة؛ للفرضية، أو لكثرة وقوعها، أو لثبوتها بالكتاب. وأصل العيد عود قلبت الواو ياء لسكونها وانكسار ما قبلها، سمي به؛ لأنه يعود كل سنة، ويجمع على أعياد ليفرق عن أعواد جمع عود يعني آلة اللهو والعود بمعنى الخشبة يجمع على عيدان. وصلاة العيدين وغيرها كتكبير التشريق ما شرعت في السنة الأولى من الهجرة كما رواه أبو داود مسنداً إلى أنس رضي الله عنه، قال: قدم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم المدينة ولهم يومان يلعبون فيهما فقال: "ما هذان اليومان؟" قالوا: كنا نلعب فيهما في الجاهلية، فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: "إن الله أبدلكم بهما خيراً منهما يوم الأضحى، ويوم الفطر". تجب صلاة العيد عند الجمهور وهو الصحيح، وقيل: تسن، وبه قال الشافعي ومالك، وعن أحمد فرض كفاية. لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَانْحَرْ﴾ المراد به صلاة العيد، وكذا المراد بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِتُكَبِّرُوا اللهَ عَلَى مَا هَدَاكُمْ﴾ في تأويل، وقد واظب عليها عليه الصلاة والسلام من غير ترك، وهو دليل الوجوب. وهذا رواية الحسن عن الإمام، وهو المختار عند الجمهور، وذكر في الجامع الصغير: عيدان إذا اجتمعا في يوم واحد فالأول سنة والثاني فريضة، ولا يترك واحد منهما. ووجه سنيتها: قوله عليه في حديث الأعرابي عقيب سؤاله: هل علي غيرهن؟ قال: "لا، إلا أن تطوع". والأول أصح، وتسميتها بالسنة للوجوب بالسنة. اعلم أن لها شرائط للأداء، وشرائط للوجوب، وشرائط للجواز. فبقوله: "على من تجب" بين شرائط الوجوب أي الحر المقيم الصحيح المذكر مع سلامة البصر وقدرة المشي، وبين شرائط الأداء بقوله: "بشرائطها سوى الخطبة" وهي المصر، والسلطان، والجماعة. وشروط الجواز هي: الطهارة، وستر العورة، واستقبال القبلة، والوقت، والنية. والخطبة ليست من شرائطها؛ لأنها تؤدى بعد الصلاة، وشرط الشيء يسبقه أو يقارنه. فلا تجب على المسافر والعبد وإن أذن له مولاه، والمريض، والمرأة. سوى الخطبة فإنها ليست بشرط في العيد بخلاف الجمعة.
Chapter on the Two Eid Prayers: i.e., explaining their rulings. The Eid prayer is obligatory upon those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, with its conditions except the sermon. The connection between the two chapters is that Jumu'ah is an 'Eid; due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Indeed for every believer in every month there are four or five Eids' or due to their sharing the aforementioned conditions except the sermon, or because both are performed with a large congregation during the day, and the recitation is aloud in both, or because it is obligatory upon those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory. Jumu'ah was given precedence due to its being fard, or due to its frequent occurrence, or due to its establishment by the Book. The root of 'Eid is 'awd (return), the waw was changed to ya due to its sukun and the kasrah before it. It is named so because it returns every year. Its plural is a'yad to differentiate from a'wad, plural of 'ud meaning a musical instrument, while 'ud meaning wood has the plural 'idan. The Eid prayers and other things like the takbir of tashriq were legislated in the first year of the Hijrah, as narrated by Abu Dawud with a chain to Anas, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Prophet, peace be upon him, arrived in Madinah and they had two days in which they played. He said: 'What are these two days?' They said: 'We used to play on them during the Jahiliyyah.' He, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed Allah has replaced them for you with two better days: the Day of Adha and the Day of Fitr.' The Eid prayer is obligatory according to the majority, and this is the correct view. It is said it is sunnah, and this is the view of al-Shafi'i and Malik, and from Ahmad it is fard kifayah. Due to His saying, exalted: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' – the intended meaning is the Eid prayer, and similarly the intended meaning of His saying: 'And so that you may magnify Allah for having guided you' in one interpretation. And he, peace be upon him, consistently performed it without ever leaving it, and this is evidence of obligation. This is the narration of al-Hasan from the Imam, and it is the chosen view according to the majority. It is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'If two Eids coincide on the same day, the first is sunnah and the second is fard, and neither is to be omitted.' The basis for its being sunnah is his saying, peace be upon him, in the hadith of the Bedouin after his question: 'Are there any others upon me?' He said: 'No, unless you volunteer.' The first view is more correct, and calling it sunnah is due to its being obligatory by the Sunnah. Know that it has conditions for performance, conditions for obligation, and conditions for validity. By his saying 'upon those upon whom it is obligatory', he explained the conditions of obligation: i.e., free, resident, healthy, male, with intact eyesight and ability to walk. He explained the conditions of performance by his saying 'with its conditions except the sermon': i.e., the metropolis, the ruler, and the congregation. The conditions of validity are: purity, covering the awrah, facing the qiblah, time, and intention. The sermon is not among its conditions because it is performed after the prayer, whereas the condition of a thing precedes or accompanies it. Thus it is not obligatory upon the traveler, the slave even if his master permits him, the sick, and the woman. Except the sermon: it is not a condition in the Eid unlike Jumu'ah.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the obligation and conditions of the Eid prayer. The author begins by stating that Eid prayer is obligatory upon the same people who are obligated to attend Jumu'ah, with the same conditions except the khutbah (sermon). He then explains the connection between the chapters on Jumu'ah and Eid, noting that Jumu'ah is also called 'Eid. The linguistic root of 'Eid is 'awd (return), and the prayer was legislated in the first year of Hijrah, supported by the hadith of Anas where the Prophet replaced the two days of play with Eid al-Adha and Eid al-Fitr. The passage then discusses the difference of opinion on the legal status of Eid prayer: the majority (including the Hanafi school, on the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa) hold it is wajib. Al-Shafi'i and Malik consider it sunnah, and Ahmad considers it fard kifayah. The author favors the wajib view, citing the verse 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' and the Prophet's continuous practice. He also mentions the ruling in al-Jami' al-Saghir about two Eids coinciding. Then he distinguishes three types of conditions: shurut al-wujub (conditions of obligation: being free, resident, healthy, male, sight, ability to walk), shurut al-ada' (conditions of performance: city, ruler, congregation), and shurut al-jawaz (conditions of validity: purity, covering awrah, facing qiblah, time, intention). Notably, the khutbah is not a condition for Eid because it comes after the prayer. Finally, he lists those exempted: traveler, slave, sick, and women.

Key Terms
صلاة العيد (Salat al-'Eid): The congregational prayer performed on the mornings of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha
شروط الوجوب (Shurut al-wujub): Conditions that make the prayer obligatory: freedom, residence, health, masculinity, sight, ability to walk
شروط الأداء (Shurut al-ada'): Conditions for proper performance: being in a metropolis, presence of ruler, congregation
شرائط الجواز (Sharait al-jawaz): Conditions for validity: purity, covering awrah, facing qiblah, time, intention

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for the obligation of Eid prayer?
A) Being male
B) Being free
C) Being resident in a city with a ruler
D) Being healthy

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib upon free, resident, healthy adult males with sight and ability to walk; its performance requires a city, ruler, and congregation; its validity requires purity and facing qiblah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Sunnah Acts and Timing of Eid Prayer
Lists recommended acts before Eid prayer, takbir dispute, nafl prohibition, time window

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts before Eid prayer, identify the Hanafi ruling on takbir and nafl, and determine the valid time for Eid prayer.

Core Idea
Eid prayer requires sunnah preparations, a disputed takbir, a disliked nafl, and a time from sunrise to zawal.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq lists the recommended acts before the Eid prayer, clarifies the internal Hanafi dispute on whether to say takbir aloud or quietly, establishes the dislike of performing voluntary prayer before the Eid prayer, and defines the time window from sunrise to midday. Understanding these details ensures one performs the Eid prayer correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the sunnah acts
List the recommended acts mentioned: eating an odd number of dates or sweets, performing ghusl, using miswak, applying perfume, wearing best clothes, paying sadaqat al-fitr, walking to the musalla, returning by a different route, and greeting with 'Taqabbal Allah minna wa minkum'.
These are sunnah, not obligatory.
2
Identify the dispute over takbir
Recognize that Imam Abu Hanifa holds takbir should be said quietly (sirr), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold it should be aloud (jahr). The evidence for each is provided in the text.
The disagreement is about the original ruling; quiet takbir is agreed upon as permissible.
3
Determine the ruling on nafl before Eid
Understand that performing voluntary prayer (nafl) before the Eid prayer is disliked (makruh) for both the imam and the congregation, in the musalla or elsewhere.
This is contrary to the Shafi'i position that it is only disliked for the imam.
4
Define the time for Eid prayer
State that the time is from sunrise (after the disliked time) to zawal (when the sun passes the meridian). If zawal enters while one is still praying, the prayer is invalid by agreement if before sitting for tashahhud; after sitting, Imam says invalid, Sahibayn say valid.
The beginning of the time is after sunrise to avoid the disliked time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن يطعم: أي يأكل قبل الخروج إلى المصلى تميرات ثلاثاً أو خمساً، وأن يكون وتراً، وشيئاً من أي حلو كان بذلك ورد الأثر. ويغتسل ويستاك ويتطيب ويلبس أحسن ثيابه ويؤدي صدقة الفطر، ثم يتوجه إلى المصلى غير مكبر ومتنفل قبلها. ووقتها من ارتفاع الشمس إلى زوالها. ويغتسل: الأصح أنه سنة، وسماه مندوباً لاشتمال السنة عليه. ومن المستحب إظهار الفرح والبشاشة وإكثار الصدقة حسب الطاقة وصلاة الغداة في مسجد حيه، والخروج ماشياً والرجوع من طريق آخر، والتهنئة بـ "تقبل الله منا ومنكم"، وكذا المصافحة. ويستحب أن يتوجه ماشياً؛ لأنه عليه السلام ما ركب في عيد ولا جنازة، ولا بأس بالركوب في الرجوع؛ لأنه غير قاصد إلى قربة. أحسن ثيابه: ولو غسيلاً؛ لأنه يوم اجتماع وسرور. أي أجملها جديداً أو غسيلاً؛ لأنه عليه السلام كان يلبس بردة حمراء في كل عيد. ويتطيب بما له ريح لا لون كالمسك والبخور. ويؤدي صدقة الفطر: الحديث عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه قال: "أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بزكاة الفطر أن نؤديها قبل خروج الناس إلى الصلاة"؛ لأن في أدائه للفقير إعانة له ليفرغ قلبه للصلاة. ثم يتوجه إلخ بالنصب بتقدير "أن" معطوف على المندوبات قبله، فاقتضى ندبه أيضاً كما في المجتبى: الخروج إلى المصلى لصلاة العيد سنة، وإن كان يسعهم المسجد الجامع عند عامة المشائخ وهو الصحيح، ولا بأس بإخراج المنبر إليها، واختلف في كراهة بنائه فيها، فقيل: يكره، وقيل: لا، وعن الإمام لا بأس به. المصلى وهو الموضع الذي يجتمع فيه الناس مع الإمام لصلاة. غير مكبر: أي حال كونه غير مكبر جهراً في الطريق بل مكبراً خفية؛ لأن التكبير غير موضوع لا خلاف في جوازه بصفة الإخفاء، وإليه ذهب الإمام؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاذْكُرْ رَبَّكَ فِي نَفْسِكَ﴾، وقال علي: "خير الذكر الخفي"؛ ولأن الأصل في الثناء الإخفاء، إلا ما خصه الشرع في يوم الأضحى. وقالا: يكبر جهراً؛ لما روي أن ابن عمر كان يرفع صوته بالتكبير، وهو مروي عن علي رضي الله عنه. وقيل: الخلاف في أصل التكبير، فعنده لا يكبر، وعندهما يكبر. ومتنفل قبلها: أي يكره التنفل قبل صلاة العيد مطلقاً في حق الإمام والقوم وفي المصلى وغيره. وقال الشافعي: يكره في حق الإمام لا في حق القوم. وقيل: غير مكروه، والجمهور على الكراهة في المصلى وغيرها؛ لما ورد عنه عليه السلام من المنع عن التنفل في العيدين قبل الإمام، ولأنه عليه السلام لم يفعل ذلك مع حرصه على الصلاة. وقبلها: قبل صلاة العيد لكراهته في حق الإمام والقوم في المصلى وغيره. إلى زوالها: أي الشمس عن كبد السماء. وقال الشافعي: وقتها طلوع الشمس ويستحب تأخيرها. الغاية غير داخلة حتى لو دخل وقت الزوال وهو فيها فسدت الصلاة اتفاقاً إن كان قبل أن يقعد قدر التشهد، أما بعده قبل السلام فكذا عند الإمام خلافاً لهما. ابتداء الوقت من ارتفاع الشمس ليخرج الوقت عن حد الكراهة.
He should eat: i.e., he should eat before going out to the musalla three or five dates, and they should be odd, and a bit of any sweet thing - thus the tradition has come. He should perform ghusl, use a miswak, apply perfume, wear his best clothes, pay sadaqat al-fitr, then proceed to the musalla without saying takbir aloud and without performing nafl before it. Its time is from the rising of the sun to its zenith. Ghusl: the sounder view is that it is sunnah, and it is called recommended because the sunnah includes it. Among the recommended acts are showing joy and cheerfulness, giving much charity according to capacity, performing the morning prayer in the mosque of his neighborhood, going out walking, returning by another route, greeting with 'May Allah accept from us and from you,' and likewise shaking hands. It is recommended to go walking because he, peace be upon him, never rode on an Eid nor a funeral. There is no harm in riding on the return because he is not intending an act of worship. His best clothes: even if washed, because it is a day of gathering and joy. i.e., the finest, new or washed, because he, peace be upon him, used to wear a red cloak on every Eid. And apply perfume that has scent but no color, like musk and incense. And pay sadaqat al-fitr: the hadith of Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, ordered us to give zakat al-fitr before the people went out to the prayer' because paying it to the poor helps him free his heart for prayer. Then proceed etc.: with nasb by implied 'an', conjoined to the recommended acts before it, so it is also recommended as in al-Mujtaba: going out to the musalla for Eid prayer is sunnah, even if the congregational mosque can accommodate them, according to the majority of mashayikh, and this is correct. There is no harm in taking the minbar out to it. There is difference of opinion regarding the dislike of building one there: some say it is disliked, some say no, and from the Imam there is no harm. The musalla is the place where people gather with the imam for prayer. Without saying takbir aloud: i.e., not saying it aloud on the way, rather saying it quietly. Because the takbir is not a problematic matter; there is no disagreement about the permissibility of doing it quietly. The Imam held this view due to His saying: 'And remember your Lord within yourself' and Ali said: 'The best remembrance is the hidden one.' And the principle is that praise should be hidden except where the Law specifies it for the day of Adha. The two said: he should say it aloud, based on the report that Ibn Umar used to raise his voice with takbir, and it is reported from Ali. Some say the disagreement is about the original takbir: according to him (Imam) he does not say it, according to them (the two) he does. And without performing nafl before it: i.e., it is disliked to perform nafl before Eid prayer absolutely, for the imam and the people, in the musalla and elsewhere. Al-Shafi'i said: it is disliked for the imam but not for the people. Some say it is not disliked. The majority hold that it is disliked in the musalla and elsewhere due to the prohibition from him, peace be upon him, regarding nafl on the two Eids before the imam, and because he, peace be upon him, did not do it despite his eagerness for prayer. Before it: before Eid prayer, due to its dislike for the imam and the people in the musalla and elsewhere. To its zenith: i.e., the sun away from the middle of the sky. Al-Shafi'i said: its time is from sunrise and it is recommended to delay it. The end is not included, so if the time of zawal enters while one is in the prayer, the prayer is invalidated by agreement if it occurs before sitting for the amount of tashahhud. As for after it before the salams, it is thus according to the Imam, contrary to the two. The beginning of the time is from the rising of the sun to remove the time from the level of dislike.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage details the sunnah acts before Eid prayer and the ruling on its time. The author lists recommended acts: eating an odd number of dates (or sweets) before Eid al-Fitr, performing ghusl, using miswak, applying perfume, wearing best clothes (new or washed), and paying sadaqat al-fitr before going out. It is recommended to walk to the musalla, return by a different route, and greet with 'Taqabbal Allah minna wa minkum.' Regarding takbir on the way, there is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions: Imam says to recite quietly, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say aloud. The passage also clarifies that voluntary prayer (nafl) before Eid prayer is disliked for both the imam and congregation, a view opposed by al-Shafi'i. Finally, the time for Eid prayer is from sunrise to midday. If one begins the prayer and zawal enters before sitting for tashahhud, the prayer is invalid; if after sitting, Imam says it is invalid while the two companions differ. The beginning of the time is after sunrise to avoid the disliked time.

Key Terms
المصلى (al-Musalla): The place outside the mosque where the Eid prayer is performed
التكبير (al-Takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' on the day of Eid, either quietly or aloud
وقت الزوال (Waqt al-Zawal): The time when the sun passes the meridian, marking the end of the Eid prayer time

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Mustahabb (recommended)
B) Makruh (disliked) for both imam and congregation
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Makruh for the imam only

Key Takeaway
The Eid prayer has specific sunnah preparations, a disputed ruling on takbir, a disliked nafl, and a time from sunrise to zawal.

Salah — Prayer

Recommended Acts Before Eid Prayer and Their Proofs
Describes the recommended acts before Eid prayer with proofs and disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the recommended acts before Eid prayer, explain the evidence for quiet takbir, and identify the Hanafi position on nafl before Eid.

Core Idea
Eid preparation combines sunan and wajib — but the manner of takbir and nafl before prayer are matters of scholarly difference.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq details the sunan and mustahabbat that the Hanafi school recommends before the Eid prayer. Beyond the physical preparation (ghusl, clothes, perfume), it addresses the timing of sadaqat al-fitr and two debated issues: whether to recite takbir aloud or quietly on the way to prayer, and whether to pray nafl before the Eid prayer. The text provides proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and resolves the intra-Hanafi differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List the acts mentioned: ghusl, siwak, perfume, best clothes, sadaqat al-fitr, walking to musalla, returning via different route, greeting with 'Taqabbal Allah'.
These are sunnah or mustahabb, except sadaqat al-fitr which is wajib.
2
Classify each act's legal status
Determine which are sunnah (ghusl, clothes, walking), mustahabb (perfume, greeting), and wajib (sadaqat al-fitr).
Use the commentary to confirm the hukm level.
3
Examine the takbir dispute
Abu Hanifa says takbir quietly based on Quran 7:205 and hadith 'Khayr al-dhikr al-khafi'; Sahibayn say aloud based on Ibn Umar's practice.
The mufta bihi is quiet recitation.
4
Examine the nafl dispute
Hanafi: nafl before Eid is makruh for both imam and congregation; Shafi'i: only for imam. The majority hold absolute dislike.
The text cites the Prophet's practice as evidence.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
A person should prepare physically, give charity before the prayer, walk quietly, and avoid any nafl prayer before the Eid prayer.
If the imam commands otherwise, obedience is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
باب صلاة العيدين
ويغتسل ويستاك ويتطيب ويلبس أحسن ثيابه ويؤدي صدقة الفطر، ثم يتوجه إلى
المصلى غير مكبر ومتنفل قبلها.
ويغتسل: الأصح أنه سنة، وسماه مندوباً لاشتمال السنة عليه، ومن المستحب إظهار الفرح والبشاشة وإكثار الصدقة حسب الطاقة وصلاة الغداة في مسجد حيه، والخروج ماشيا والرجوع من طريق آخر، والتهنئة بـ"تقبل الله منا ومنكم"، وكذا المصافحة، ويستحب أن يتوجه ماشيا؛ لأنه عليه ما ركب في عيد ولا جنازة ولا بأس بالركوب في الرجوع؛ لأنه غير قاصد إلى قربة. (فتح) أحسن ثيابه: [ولو غسيلا؛ لأنه . يوم اجتماع وسرور. (ط، ع] أي أجملها جديداً أو غسيلاً؛ لأنه عليه كان يلبس بردة حمراء في كل عيد. (فتح) ويتطيب بما له ريح لا لون كالمسك والبخور. (ط) ويؤدي صدقة الفطر: الحديث ابن عمر لما أنه قال: "أمرنا رسول الله [؟] بزكاة الفطر أن نؤديها قبل خروج الناس إلى الصلاة" كشف الحقائق: ۸۳/۱]؛ لأن في أدائه للفقير إعانة له ليفرغ قلبه للصلاة. (فتح) ثم يتوجه إلخ بالنصب بتقدير "أن" معطوف على المندوبات قبله، فاقتضى ندبه أيضاً كما في المجتبى: الخروج إلى المصلى لصلاة العيد سنة، وإن كان يسعهم المسجد الجامع عند عامة المشائخ وهو الصحيح، ولا بأس بإخراج المنبر إليها، واختلف في كراهة بنائه فيها، فقيل: يكره، وقيل: لا، وعن الإمام لا بأس به. (فتح) المصلى وهو الموضع الذي يجتمع فيه الناس مع الإمام لصلاة. (ع) غير مكبر: [ أي حال كونه غير مكبر جهراً في الطريق بل مكبرا خفية. (ع)] أي جهراً؛ لأن التكبير غير موضوع لا خلاف في جوازه بصفة الإخفاء، وإليه ذهب الإمام؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاذْكُرْ رَبَّكَ فِي نَفْسِكَ﴾ (الأعراف:٢٠٥)، وقال علي: "خير الذكر الخفي"؛ ولأن الأصل في الثناء الإخفاء، إلا ما خصه الشرع في يوم الأضحى، وقالا: يكبر جهراً؛ لما روي أن ابن عمر لما كان يرفع صوته بالتكبير، وهو مروي عن علي له وقيل: الخلاف في أصل التكبير، فعنده لا يكبر، وعندهما يكبر. (فتح) ومتنفل قبلها: [بالجر عطف على مكبر أي وغير متنفل (ع)] أي يكره التنفل قبل صلاة العيد مطلقاً في حق الإمام والقوم وفي المصلى وغيره، وقال الشافعي يكره في حق الإمام لا في حق القوم، وقيل: غير مكروه، والجمهور على الكراهة في المصلى وغيرها؛ لما ورد عنه عليه من المنع عن التنفل في العيدين قبل الإمام، ولأنه عليه لم يفعل ذلك مع حرصه على الصلاة مسكين) ومستخلص قبلها قبل صلاة العيد لكراهته في حق الإمام والقوم في المصلّي وغيره. (ط)
Book of Prayer, Chapter of the Two Eid Prayers. He performs ghusl, uses siwak, applies perfume, wears his best clothes, gives sadaqat al-fitr, then proceeds to the musalla, not reciting takbir loudly and not performing any nafl prayer before it. [Commentary] Ghusl: the correct view is that it is sunnah, and he called it mandub because it is included in the sunnah. Among the recommended acts are showing joy and cheerfulness, giving abundant charity according to one's capacity, performing the morning prayer in the mosque of his neighborhood, going out walking and returning by another route, greeting with 'May Allah accept from us and from you', and likewise handshake. It is recommended to go walking because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not ride on an Eid or a funeral, but it is permissible to ride when returning because he is not intending a devotional act. (Fath) Best clothes: [even if washed] because it is a day of gathering and joy. (T, A) meaning the most beautiful, new or washed, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to wear a red cloak on every Eid. (Fath) Perfume: with something that has a scent but no color, like musk and incense. (T) He gives sadaqat al-fitr: the hadith of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah ordered us regarding zakat al-fitr to give it before the people go out to the prayer.' (Kashf al-Haqaiq: 83/1) because giving it to the poor helps them to free their hearts for prayer. (Fath) Then he proceeds etc.: with nasb by assuming 'an' coordinated with the recommended acts before it, so it is also recommended. As in al-Mujtaba: going out to the musalla for Eid prayer is sunnah, even if the congregational mosque accommodates them, according to the majority of mashayikh, and this is the correct view. There is no harm in taking the minbar out to it. There is a difference of opinion on the dislike of building a minbar there: some said it is disliked, others said no, and from Imam Abu Hanifa: there is no harm. (Fath) Al-Musalla: the place where people gather with the Imam for prayer. (A) Not saying takbir loudly: [i.e., being in a state of not saying takbir loudly in the street, rather saying it quietly. (A)] meaning loudly, because there is no disagreement on the permissibility of saying it quietly. Imam Abu Hanifa held this due to the verse {And remember your Lord within yourself} (al-A'raf 205), and Ali said: 'The best remembrance is the hidden one', and because the original concerning praise is concealment, except what the Law specifies on the day of Adha. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he says takbir loudly, based on the report that Ibn Umar would raise his voice with takbir, and it is also reported from Ali. It is said that the disagreement is about the essence of takbir: according to him (Abu Hanifa) he does not say it, according to them he says it. (Fath) Not performing nafl before it: [with jar, coordinated with 'mukabbir', i.e., and not performing nafl (A)] meaning it is disliked to perform nafl before Eid prayer absolutely, for the Imam and the congregation, in the musalla or elsewhere. Al-Shafi'i said: it is disliked for the Imam only, not for the congregation. Some said it is not disliked. The majority hold it disliked in the musalla and elsewhere, due to the prohibition reported from him (peace be upon him) regarding nafl on the two Eids before the Imam, and because he (peace be upon him) did not do it despite his eagerness for prayer. And a summary: it is disliked for the Imam and the congregation in the musalla and elsewhere. (T)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage lists the recommended acts (sunan and mustahabbat) before the Eid prayer. The commentary clarifies each: Ghusl is sunnah, not wajib. Smiling, charity, walking to the musalla, returning via a different route, and greeting with 'Taqabbal Allah' are recommended. The Prophet's practice of wearing a red cloak (burdah hamra') on Eid shows the excellence of good clothes. Perfume should have scent but no color. Sadaqat al-fitr must be given before the prayer to enable the poor to pray. There is a range of opinions on walking vs. riding: walking is preferred for going, riding permissible for return. The takbir on the way: Imam Abu Hanifa prefers silently based on the Quranic verse, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) prefer aloud based on Ibn Umar's practice; the difference is whether one says takbir at all or only audibly. Nafl prayer before Eid is disliked for everyone, according to the Hanafi school, unlike Shafi'i who restricts the dislike to the Imam. The passage emphasizes the social and spiritual preparation for the Eid prayer.

Key Terms
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Charity given on Eid al-Fitr before the prayer, wajib on every free Muslim who owns nisab.
مكبر (mukabbir): One who says takbir (Allahu Akbar). Here, referring to saying takbir aloud during the walk to the prayer.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One who performs a nafl (supererogatory) prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is sunnah
B) It is makruh for both Imam and congregation
C) It is permissible only for the congregation
D) It is wajib for the Imam

Key Takeaway
Preparation for Eid prayer includes sunnan acts and wajib sadaqat; the manner of takbir and forbearance from nafl follow the Hanafi school's preferred positions.

The Valid Time for Eid Prayer in the Hanafi School
Defines the time window for Eid prayer and its limits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the start and end times of Eid prayer, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on zawal entering during prayer, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Eid prayer time begins after sunrise by a spear's length and ends at zawal; if zawal enters after tashahhud, the prayer is valid.

This lesson examines the prescribed time for Eid prayer in the Hanafi school. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq establishes the time window and addresses an important edge case: what if the sun reaches its zenith while the prayer is still in progress? The commentary resolves the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point, giving the mufta bihi ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووقتها من ارتفاع الشمس إلى زوالها . الشمس إلى زوالها : [قدر رمح أو رمحين. ] أي الشمس عن كبد السماء، وقال الشافعي: وقتها طلوع الشمس ويستحب تأخيرها رمز الحقائق: ۱۰۲/۱] الغاية غير داخلة حتى لو دخل وقت الزوال وهو فيها فسدت الصلاة اتفاقاً إن كان قبل أن يقعد قدر التشهد أما بعده قبل السلام فكذا عند الإمام خلافاً لهما، وابتداء الوقت من ارتفاع الشمس ليخرج الوقت عن حد الكراهة. (فتح)
And its time is from the rising of the sun until its declining. [Commentary] The sun until its declining: about a spear's length or two. Meaning the sun from the midsky. Al-Shafi'i said: its time is from sunrise, and it is recommended to delay it. (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 102/1) The end is not included, so if the time of zawal enters while one is in the prayer, the prayer becomes invalid by agreement if it occurs before sitting for the duration of tashahhud. After that, before the taslim, it is the same according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The beginning of the time is from the rising of the sun so that the time exits the limit of dislike. (Fath)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage specifies the valid time for Eid prayer: it begins when the sun has risen above the horizon by about one or two spear-lengths (approximately 15-20 minutes after sunrise) and continues until just before zawal (when the sun reaches its zenith and begins to decline). The end time is exclusive: if one starts the prayer and enters the zawal time before completing the prayer, the prayer is invalid if the zawal occurs before the person sits for tashahhud. If after tashahhud but before salam, Abu Hanifa says it also invalidates, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the prayer is valid. The majority of hadith and practice support starting after sunrise to avoid the disliked time of sunrise itself. Note that the Shafi'i school allows Eid prayer from sunrise itself, but Hanafis prefer the delay to avoid the time of karahah.

Key Terms
ارتفاع الشمس (irtifa' al-shams): The sun rising to the height of a spear above the horizon.
زوال (zawal): The sun's decline from its zenith; the start of the time for Zuhr prayer.
تشهد (tashahhud): The sitting and recitation of the testimony of faith in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the beginning time for Eid prayer?
A) At sunrise
B) After the sun has risen by a spear's length
C) After zawal
D) Anytime before noon

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rulings on Eid prayer time: begin after ishraq, end at zawal; if zawal enters after tashahhud, prayer is valid.
